And only when we see a special effort by the donor to participate in the Mishkan’s donation by bringing all the types, "blue, and purple, and scarlet wool, etc.," then he is trusted that he also exerted himself and dyed the wool "for His sake."
And this is what Rashi negates in his explanation, "and every man with whom was found blue, or purple, or scarlet wool, etc."—that the intent of the verses is not that they brought all the types, but that it means "or, or."

It can be said that the proof that the act of preparation (in dyeing the wool, etc.) was "for His sake" is from the fact that everyone who had any of these items (even only one of them) brought them to the Mishkan, and brought everything he had of these items (and not like the brooches, nose-rings, etc., all gold jewelry, where it is not said that they brought all the jewelry and gold they had), and this is sufficient proof that the act of preparation was in the manner of "for Me, for My sake".

6. It can be said that on this matter, Rashi (on the Torah) and the Midrash differ:
It is stated in the Midrash: "Yaakov Avinu... called his sons and said to them: Know that the Holy One, blessed be He, will in the future tell your children to make a Mishkan; therefore, let all its needs be prepared in your hands, etc. And there were those among them who prepared themselves for the items, and there were those who forgot. And when Moshe came and they made the Mishkan, there were those who brought from their own, and there were those who brought only from what was lying in their hand, for so it says, 'every man with whom was found blue and purple,' and it says 'all with whom was found acacia wood.'" The commentators explain that in the two aforementioned verses it is written "with whom was found" (regarding blue and purple, etc., and regarding acacia wood), which means that it was kept ready for them from their ancestors—unlike regarding the brooches and nose-rings and all gold jewelry and the like, where it is said that it was with the generosity of heart of the donor (not that it was prepared beforehand, from their ancestors).

But Rashi does not explain "with whom was found" stated regarding blue and purple, etc., as meaning that it was ready for them from their ancestors, and if so, he holds that they prepared and separated these types for Hashem.

It can be said that it depends on the definition of the law of "for His sake" that was required in the donation of the Mishkan, for one can say there are two ways to view this: a) that it is a law regarding the action of the person (*maaseh hagevra*), or b) that it is a matter that belongs to and is attached to the object (*cheftza*), that this object must be made "for His sake."

And herein lies the difference between the Midrash and Rashi’s explanation:
According to the Midrash, the requirement of "for His sake" in the Mishkan’s donation relates to the holiness of the items from which the Mishkan was made, for in order for there to be "and I will dwell among them," within the items in the Mishkan, the items must be prepared for their holiness. That is, it concerns the very essence of the object of these items, that they be ready for the work of the Mishkan. Therefore, the Midrash explains that when it says "with whom was found blue and purple, etc.," it means that these items were already prepared by the Bnei Yisrael for the work of the Mishkan, because for these items that required preparation, there was a special command from Yaakov Avinu that their needs be prepared in their hands, so that they could be sure that the items would be made from their beginning (i.e., also during the act of preparation) "for My sake," for the sake of the Mishkan, and then they could bring them to the Mishkan.

Whereas for Rashi, the requirement of "for My sake" is a law regarding the action of the person (*maaseh hagevra*), for since the making of the Mishkan is connected with the atonement for the sin of the Calf (in which it was evident that Hashem had forgiven them for the sin of the Calf, as mentioned above), therefore it was required that their donation to Hashem be "for Me—for My sake" (the opposite of their giving to the Golden Calf).

Therefore, it is impossible for Rashi to explain "with whom was found" as meaning that these items were already prepared for safekeeping from their ancestors (for then there is no intention of "for His sake" on the part of the person donating), but rather it refers to the donors themselves, that they prepared and separated these types "for His sake."

7. Now, based on all the above, the difference we find between the men and the women in the donation of the Mishkan will be understood—that although the men also donated to the Mishkan with generosity of heart, nevertheless, they brought only what was required of them, i.e., the items themselves of "blue, and purple, and scarlet wool, etc.," whereas the women, not only did they donate to the work of the Mishkan even more than the men, as it is written "and the men came upon the women", but furthermore, they did not settle for bringing the items themselves, but brought spun material (for which they also spun the blue, and the purple, and the scarlet wool, and the fine linen themselves, and likewise "spun the goats’ hair").

And based on the above, one can say a reason for this also according to Halacha:
For the men, they could not permit them to bring spun material, because after they sinned with the Calf, there is no certain trust that they would perform their work "for His sake", and they could trust the "wise-hearted" whom Hashem "filled with wisdom of heart";
Whereas the women, they did not participate in the sin of the Calf, and consequently, there is no room at all for doubt regarding the action and work of "for Me, for My sake"—for certainly, among them there is the utmost generosity of heart for all matters of holiness, and especially in matters of the Mishkan, as was the case in practice, that they did not withhold themselves from any exertion so that their donation would be more beautiful, to the point that for this reason—"they spun the goats’ hair," "from off the goats they spun them", because of the greatness of their generosity of heart for the matters of the Mishkan, they also exerted themselves with "extra craftsmanship" in the work of the Mishkan.

(From the Sicha of Shabbos Parshas Vayakhel-Pekudei, 5747)

## Sicha 3

### 211

**A.** Regarding the verse, "And Moshe said to the Children of Yisrael: See, Hashem has called by name Betzalel, son of Uri, son of Chur, of the tribe of Yehudah," Rashi explains: "Chur was the son of Miriam."

We must understand: Chur was already mentioned in the Torah earlier (at the end of Parshas Beshalach) in the war against Amalek ("And Moshe, Aharon, and Chur went up to the top of the hill," and "Aharon and Chur supported his [Moshe's] hands"), and also at the end of Parshas Mishpatim—where it is told that when Moshe went up to the mountain, he said to the elders, "Aharon and Chur are with you, etc." In both places, Rashi explains that Chur "was the son of Miriam." If so, why does Rashi need to repeat this in our Parsha?

The commentators explain Rashi’s intent: "It is difficult, for it is not the way to trace a person’s lineage only to his father, as he traced Oholiav [to his father], so why did he trace Betzalel to Chur, his grandfather? Rather, it must be that Chur (being the son of Miriam) was the primary lineage of Betzalel, and therefore he traces him after him."

But seemingly, this is not a sufficient answer, because:
1) In our Parsha, it speaks of Moshe’s words to the Children of Yisrael (regarding the appointment of Betzalel, etc.), but these same matters were already stated earlier in Parshas Tetzaveh in the words of Hashem to Moshe: "And Hashem spoke to Moshe, saying: See, I have called by name Betzalel, son of Uri, son of Chur, of the tribe of

## 212

Yehudah," and there Rashi did not explain anything. If Rashi is bothered by why he traces Betzalel to his grandfather, he should have explained it earlier in Parshas Tetzaveh.

2) Even if you say that "Chur was the primary lineage of Betzalel," what is Rashi’s proof that the reason the verse traces him to Chur is because he was the son of Miriam (which is not mentioned in the verse)? It could simply be said that this is due to the greatness of Chur himself.

This is proven by the two aforementioned places regarding the greatness of Chur: (a) Only Aharon and Chur went up with Moshe during the war against Amalek (and especially according to Rashi there, "From here [we learn] for a fast that three are needed to pass before the ark, etc."—and Chur was one of the three); (b) When Moshe went up to the mountain, he said, "To the elders... Aharon and Chur are with you; whoever has a dispute, let him approach them"—showing that the greatness of Chur was [even] greater than the seventy elders.

Furthermore: In Rashi earlier, it is brought that at the time of the making of the Golden Calf, Chur was rebuking the Children of Yisrael and they killed him. That is to say: (a) At a time when Aharon was only striving to delay the Children of Yisrael, Chur "was rebuking them," and (b) because of this he was killed, which is the elevation of *mesiras nefesh* for *kiddush Hashem*.

If so, how does Rashi have the authority to innovate that the intent of the verse is to trace Betzalel to (Chur, being the son of) Miriam—and not to Chur himself?

**B.** It can be said that Rashi’s comment, "Chur was the son of Miriam," is not a separate statement, but rather the beginning of the Rashi that follows on the verse, "And to teach, He has placed in his heart, he and Oholiav, son of Achisamach, of the tribe of Dan," which states: "Oholiav, from the tribe of Dan, from the lower of the tribes, from the sons of the handmaids, and the Place [Hashem] made him equal to Betzalel for the work of the Mishkan, and he is from the greatest of the tribes, to fulfill what is said: 'And he does not recognize the noble before the poor.'"

That is to say: The intent of the verse in mentioning the lineage of Betzalel and Oholiav is to emphasize the distance between them—that Betzalel is "from the greatest of the tribes" and Oholiav is "from the lower of the tribes"—and yet, "the Place made him equal to Betzalel." For this reason, the verse emphasizes "son of Chur," and Rashi explains "he was the son of Miriam"—"to make known the greatness of his lineage from the greatest of lineage and

## 213

greatness, both from the side of the father and from the side of the mother, through which is fulfilled more [perfectly] what is said... 'And he does not recognize the noble, etc.'"

[It can be said that this is also in accordance with what is said regarding Oholiav, "from the lower of the tribes, from the sons of the handmaids," meaning that his inferiority pertains to the lineage of the mother, and therefore it is logical to say that the greatness of the lineage of Betzalel is (not only from the side of the father but also) from the side of the mother.]

Based on this, it is resolved why Rashi did not explain on the verse "Betzalel... son of Chur" in Parshas Tetzaveh that Chur was the son of Miriam—because in Parshas Tetzaveh, it is possible to say simply that the verse wishes to trace Betzalel to Chur due to the virtues of Chur that are explicit in the verse (and in Rashi), as mentioned in section A. Only in our Parsha, where the primary intent is to emphasize that "he does not recognize the noble before the poor," does Rashi add that the lineage to Chur comes to describe the greatness of his lineage (also) from the side of the mother, as mentioned above.

However, the question still stands: Regarding Oholiav, it was also stated earlier in Parshas Tetzaveh (in Hashem’s speech to Moshe): "And I, behold, I have given with him Oholiav, son of Achisamach, of the tribe of Dan," and there Rashi did not explain anything. If you say that the intent of the verse in mentioning the lineage of Betzalel and Oholiav is to emphasize the matter of "he does not recognize the noble before the poor," Rashi should have explained this earlier in Parshas Tetzaveh. [And indeed, it is so in the Midrash (which is the source, seemingly, of this Rashi), that the content of this matter ("that the great and the small are equal before the Holy One, Blessed be He") was brought earlier on the verses of Parshas Tetzaveh.]

And we must conclude that this is the way of the verses, to trace a person after his father and his tribe, and there is no necessity to say (according to the *peshat*) that the intent of the verse in Parshas Tetzaveh is to teach that "he does not recognize the noble before the poor"—and if so, what is the difficulty in the *peshat* of the verses of our Parsha that compelled Rashi to explain that the intent here is "to fulfill what is said: 'And he does not recognize the noble before the poor'"?

**C.** The words of the *Levush* seem correct, that Rashi is bothered by the change in the language of the verses. Above (in Parshas Tetzaveh) it is written, "And I, behold, I have given with him Oholiav, etc.," and "with him" can be interpreted to mean that He gave him *with* him (the *es*—the secondary one) to serve him in this work, not that he would be the head of the craftsmen like him. But in our Parsha, Moshe says, "To teach, He has placed in his heart, he and Oholiav," which implies that he would be equal to Betzalel in the instruction of this work to the craftsmen, that he would be a head like him. Therefore, Rashi explains here (specifically) that Oholiav is from the tribe of Dan, etc., to fulfill what is said: "He does not recognize the noble before the poor."

But it is still not understood:
What is the necessity that the fact that the Place made Oholiav equal to Betzalel is "to fulfill what

## 214

is said: 'And he does not recognize the noble before the poor,'" and that this is the reason the verse emphasizes their lineage? It is possible to say simply that the reason both were chosen to instruct and oversee the work of the Mishkan is because of the greatness of their wisdom, and that the fact that Oholiav is equal to Betzalel "in the instruction of this work to the craftsmen and he would be a head like him" is because he is equal to Betzalel in "wisdom of heart." [And on the contrary: what is the practical difference regarding the matter of lineage when it is a matter that requires "wisdom of heart"?]

Based on this, how does Rashi have the authority to innovate that the reason for their equality is "to fulfill what is said: 'And he does not recognize the noble before the poor'" [and the fact that the verse traces their lineage, etc., is not a difficulty at all, for that is the way of the verses (and in the case at hand itself, the verse traces them also earlier in Parshas Tetzaveh), as mentioned above]?

Seemingly, it is possible to answer that from the length of the verse here, it is proven that Betzalel was the primary one [meaning that in addition to the fact that in Parshas Tetzaveh the verse speaks at length only about Betzalel, and it is proven that he alone was the head of all the craftsmen, it is also implied from the verses of our Parsha that Betzalel was the primary one], for at first there is length in the verse regarding the virtue of Betzalel—"See, Hashem has called by name Betzalel, etc., and I have filled him with the spirit of Elokus, with wisdom, etc., and to think thoughts, etc., and in carving stone, etc., in all manner of skillful work," and only afterwards does the verse continue, "And to teach, He has placed in his heart, he and Oholiav, etc., He has filled them with wisdom of heart to do all manner of work of the craftsman, etc.," and it is implied from this that the wisdom of Betzalel was greater than that of Oholiav. If so, it is difficult why he made them equal regarding the matter of instructing the work? And therefore Rashi explains that it is in order "to fulfill what is said: 'And he does not recognize the noble before the poor.'"

But based on this, it is not understood from the other side: If the wisdom of Betzalel was indeed greater than that of Oholiav, how can they be made equal solely to fulfill "And he does not recognize the noble before the poor"? Just as one should not show favoritism to the rich because of his wealth, so too there is no place to show favoritism to the poor when he is not worthy of it—only to make him equal to the rich!

Also, it must be understood:
1) Why is there a need to emphasize the matter of "he does not recognize the noble before the poor" by comparing Betzalel and Oholiav (and especially since the difference between them is not a matter of "noble" and "poor" in the simple sense, but a matter of lineage)—when the content of the matter of "he does not recognize the noble before the poor" is explicit in the verse before this, and in connection with the making of the Mishkan—the commandment of the *machatzis hashekel*, in which it is explicit: "The rich shall not give more, and the poor shall not give less"? (And especially since there were two givings of the *machatzis hashekel* (one for the contribution of the sockets and one to purchase from them communal offerings) which in the language of Rashi—"the poor and the rich were made equal in them").

## 215

2) What is the precision of Rashi’s language, "to fulfill what is said, etc."—a language that is unusual in Rashi’s commentary, and he should have said, "as it is said," "and this is what is written," and the like.

**D.** It can be said that the explanation for this is:
Rashi’s intent is to answer (not only the reason that "the Place made him equal to Betzalel," but also) the reason for the change in the language of the verse between the commandment of Hashem to Moshe and the words of Moshe to the Children of Yisrael: In the commandment of Hashem, the equality of Oholiav to Betzalel was not emphasized, and specifically in the words of Moshe to the Children of Yisrael, it is explicit: "And to teach, etc., he and Oholiav, etc."

And although we find several times in the Torah that not all the details of the commandment were specified both in the words of Hashem to Moshe and in the words of Moshe to the Children of Yisrael (and in many places from the outset only one of them was stated in the Torah, either the commandment of Hashem or the words of Moshe to the Children of Yisrael)—because it is obvious that Moshe Rabbeinu transmitted all the commandments of Hashem to the Children of Yisrael, and that everything he said to the Children of Yisrael in the name of Hashem was commanded—

It is different in the case at hand, where it is not a matter of adding a detail alone, in which case it could be answered that the verse did not care to specify it twice, but rather a change in content: In Parshas Tetzaveh, the name of Oholiav was specified only together with the rest of the "wise of heart" ("And I, behold, I have given with him Oholiav, etc., and in the heart of all who are wise of heart, etc."), that although the fact that he was specified individually indicates his virtue relative to the rest of the wise of heart, there is no necessity to say that he would be equal to Betzalel to the point of being considered "a head like him" (and on the contrary, it is implied from this that he is "closer" to "all who are wise of heart"); whereas from the commandment "And to teach, etc., he and Oholiav, etc." in our Parsha, it is implied that they were both equal in the instruction of the work. And since this is so, why was this matter not stated immediately in the commandment of Hashem in Parshas Tetzaveh (and this omission gives room for the mistake that Oholiav is not equal to Betzalel)?

From this, Rashi learned that this emphasis on the equality of Oholiav to Betzalel is a matter that pertains primarily only to the knowledge of the Children of Yisrael, whereas in the body and essence of the commandment of Hashem, it does not matter (as much).

And this is what Rashi wrote: "And Oholiav, from the tribe of Dan, etc., to fulfill what is said: 'And he does not recognize the noble before the poor'"—and he is precise: "to fulfill what is said" (and he did not write "and this is what is written" and the like): Rashi’s intent is not that the reason the Holy One, Blessed be He, commanded to make Oholiav equal to Betzalel is because "he does not recognize the noble, etc."—for it is obvious that the primary importance in the appointment of heads of craftsmen is because of his being "a man wise of heart... to know how to do all the work of the service of the holy," and nothing more (and if he is not in this category, the reason of "he does not recognize, etc." will not help to appoint him as a head), and that is, that the fact that the Holy One, Blessed be He, commanded to appoint both as heads in the instruction of the work is solely because there was an equality in them due to which Oholiav is worthy to be equal to Betzalel in this; rather, that regarding the Children of Yisrael there was an additional matter here, that there was a need to "fulfill" (that is, to give "fulfillment" and validity—similar to *kiyemu vekiblu*, a document that was validated by its signatures) among the Children of Yisrael the content of the matter of "he does not recognize, etc." (as below), and therefore Moshe emphasized to the Children of Yisrael the equality of Betzalel and Oholiav despite the greatness of their distance in the matter of lineage.

## 216

**E.** Explanation of the matter:
Regarding the donation of the Mishkan, we find that it was according to the value of what each of the Children of Yisrael had, in the language of Rashi—"the hand of all was not equal in it, but each man according to what his heart prompted him." And as it is told in our Parsha regarding the different types of offerings from "that which was found with him," wave offering of gold, *techeiles* and *argaman*, etc., or "contribution of silver and copper," etc.

And seemingly this raises a question and wonder: The Mishkan is a matter that is most general and essential among the Children of Yisrael, and especially according to Rashi that the Mishkan is "a testimony to Yisrael that the Holy One, Blessed be He, forgave them for the act of the Golden Calf." And if so, how is it possible that in such a general and essential matter, a difference should be emphasized and remain forever between the rich, who took an important part in the donation of the Mishkan, and the poor, who did not have the ability to take an important part in the donation of the Mishkan?

[And only regarding the sockets (the foundation of the Mishkan) and the communal offerings were all equal (in the giving of the *machatzis hashekel*), as mentioned above.]

And it is found that the order of the making of the Mishkan through the donation of the Children of Yisrael was in a manner that gave room for the mistake that there is a difference between the Children of Yisrael in their connection to the Mishkan of Hashem (according to the level of the donation of their hearts).

However, since all the Children of Yisrael participated in the donation of the Mishkan, and each one according to the donation of the heart, the hand of all is equal in it (and the differences between them are only from the side of the quantity of the giving)—similar to Rashi, "One who gives much and one who gives little, provided he directs his heart to Heaven." But nevertheless, since in practice there are differences, this causes a weakness in the fact that all the Children of Yisrael belong equally to (the making of) the Mishkan.

And therefore, in order to correct this, there was a need "to fulfill what is said: 'And he does not recognize the noble before the poor,'" that is to say, to give "fulfillment" and validity so that the Children of Yisrael would know that all are equal in the making of the Mishkan (to nullify the weakness that was caused as a result of the donation of the Mishkan, in which the difference between the rich and the poor was emphasized).

And this was done by Moshe’s emphasis in his words to the Children of Yisrael that the work of the Mishkan was placed in the hand of Betzalel and Oholiav, that despite their distance in the matter of lineage—Betzalel was "from the greatest of the tribes" and from the family of Moshe Rabbeinu (for his grandfather was Chur—"he was the son of Miriam") and Oholiav was "from the lower of the tribes, from the sons of the handmaids"—nevertheless, the Place made them equal for the work of the Mishkan—"to fulfill what is said: 'And he does not recognize the noble before the poor,'" through which there was "fulfilled" among the Children of Yisrael the "foundation," that in the making of the Mishkan all of Yisrael are equal.

And based on this, it is also understood the reason that the equality of the Children of Yisrael in the matter of giving the *machatzis hashekel* was not enough "to fulfill what is said: 'And he does not recognize, etc.'"—because

## 217

here there was a need to nullify the weakness in this matter that was caused by (the differences in) the donation of the Mishkan, and for this they needed to emphasize the equality in the work of the Mishkan (which is done through the donations of the Children of Yisrael).

**F.** The explanation of this in the inner dimension of matters:
The reason for the fact that there were two manners of giving for the contribution of the Mishkan—the contributions in which "the poor and the rich were made equal," and the donation of the Mishkan in which "the hand of all was not equal in it, but each man according to what his heart prompted him"—is because this is in accordance with the two types of *avodah* that are in Yisrael:
There are matters in which all of Yisrael are equal, and there are matters in which each one is divided from his fellow, and in general: the performance of the *mitzvos*—for "there is one Torah and one law for all of us in the fulfillment of all the Torah and *mitzvos* in the aspect of action," and the intent of the *mitzvos*, the love of Hashem and His fear, etc., that "each and every one according to his measure," "which are according to the knowledge of Hashem that is in the mind and heart."

However, the ultimate intent is to draw the matter of unity also into the "donation of the heart" of the Children of Yisrael, that it should be felt that despite the differences that exist in this between one and his fellow, nevertheless all are equal before Him, may He be blessed. And this is hinted at in the fact that the making of the Mishkan (with the things that came in the donation of the Children of Yisrael, "each man according to what his heart prompted him")—was in a manner of "he does not recognize the noble before the poor."

And this is the reason that this matter is emphasized specifically in Moshe’s speaking to the Children of Yisrael, and not in the commandment of Hashem to Moshe—because this entire matter is to draw the matter of unity into this level in which the differences among the Children of Yisrael are seen, and there is no place to emphasize this in the commandment of Hashem to Moshe. Furthermore, in the commandment of Hashem to Moshe—it is still above the differences that are among the Children of Yisrael;
When Moshe transmits the commandment of Hashem to the Children of Yisrael, this "reaches" the level in which the differences between one man and his fellow exist, and Moshe draws into them the matter of unity, "he does not recognize the noble before the poor."


## שמות 

## 229

### Shemos

...Regarding what you wrote at the end of your letter, that since you could not find the source for the purity of the food in Mitzrayim, you brought the conventional version.

I am surprised by this, for it is understood that precisely when one finds an unusual version, there must certainly be a reliable source for it, as the concern is immediate that its innovation would arouse astonishment and questioning.

And the reason I am dwelling on this detail is, as understood from the introduction, that generally, those who look for sources for unusual versions are—most of them—satisfied with merely pointing to the specific place where the uncommon version is found. In my opinion, this is the secondary part—relative to the main point that requires explanation. And that is, that the inclusion of an uncommon version certainly has a special reason; the matter being discussed is strengthened and supported specifically by the uncommon and known version, which is not the case with the conventional version. And in the vast majority of cases, this is harder to explain than it is to find the source. Furthermore, this clarifies the matter more, by revealing how precise the author of the article or the writer of the book was, which is not the case regarding the source—for we are not dealing with fools, and when they bring a statement of our Sages, they certainly saw it in a book, etc.

From the above, it is also understood that those who wish to emend an ordinary version in place of an unusual one—even though in rare cases it is possible that the unusual version is a copyist's error—in the vast majority of cases this is not the fact. Since the author of the statement was precise in using the unusual version, the emendation is not a correction, but the opposite.

And so it is in the case at hand, where I intended precisely to bring the version in which food is mentioned, in connection with the struggle in recent times specifically regarding this matter, which has taken on distressing and even shameful forms, and most especially in Eretz Yisrael (may it be built and established), and there is no need to dwell on a painful matter, and the wise will understand.

I have elaborated on all the above, even though one does not cry out over the past, for the reason that if you find a way to correct the above in my opinion, it is worthwhile, and perhaps this too is for the good, since through the correction, the intention may be highlighted even more.

Regarding the substance of the matter, the source in the Midrash for the unusual version, which is also the source for the conventional version that "they did not change their dress and their language," is noted in the footnotes.

May it be the will that very soon we merit the fulfillment of the prophecy, "Behold, a people that dwells alone," for which the preparation and the vessel

## 230

for this [and according to the statement of our Rabbeinu HaZaken in Tanya, beginning of Chapter 37, that the ultimate perfection of the days of Moshiach, etc., depends on our deeds and our avodah throughout the duration of the galus, it is understood that a specific detail in perfection depends on a detail of this nature in our avodah, and likewise the matter of "dwelling alone" in the future depends on] the "dwelling alone" during the duration of the galus, by the fact that Bnei Yisrael are distinguished in all their affairs. And may we merit, speedily and in our days, to continue during Sefiras HaOmer the matter of longing for this, for the fulfillment of this prophecy, for longing adds strength, vitality, and light in the fulfillment of all the matters that hasten and bring closer the thing for which we long: our true and complete redemption.

[In the footnotes:]
In the notes of R. S. Buber (Pesikta d'Rav Kahana, Ch. 10), it is stated that the conventional statement "they did not change their dress" (the aforementioned conventional one) has no trace anywhere. And see also Otzar Divrei Chachamim by Rabbi Heiman, s.v. *Bizchus*. — However, the publisher noted that in the Pesikta there, in the footnotes, it is found in *Lekach Tov*, Parshas Tavo (26:5): It is noted there that their dress, their food, and their language were different from the Egyptians. And note the *Mei'am Loez* on the aforementioned verse, "Behold, a people that dwells alone." And see also the *Miluim* to *Torah Shleimah*, Parshas Shemos, p. 239.
(From a letter of 7 Iyar, 5717)

...And regarding the level of Moshe in the five levels called *nefesh, ruach, neshamah, chayah, yechidah*, see the writings of the Arizal as noted below. There is also found there a long explanation on the matter of "he turned aside to see," and regarding the verse "I will turn aside now and see," the *sicha* printed on this from the Rebbe, our master and teacher, of blessed memory, is well known.
(From a letter of 25 Teves, 5719)

...At the end of the book is an explanation of the Midrash in Koheles Rabbah (8:5) on the verse "He who keeps a mitzvah, etc., a wise heart."

And in Yalkut Shimoni (and see also Koheles Zuta), the Midrash is found in greater detail (and the words of Torah are poor in one place and rich in another). And it interprets the verse regarding Aharon and Moshe, Yehoshua and Moshe, Esther and Mordechai.

## 231

A commentary is also brought there that it refers to Yosef, but this commentary is only on the beginning of the verse, whereas the aforementioned commentary explains the entire verse—

From this it is certain (especially from the commentary of Yehoshua and Moshe) that the interpretation of our Sages is that the "wise man" of the verse is greater than "he who keeps a mitzvah."

It can be explained briefly that Moshe and Aharon are the "best man of the King" and "the best man of the Queen." Moshe and Yehoshua are "the face of the sun and the face of the moon," the one who bestows and the one who receives. And likewise Mordechai and Esther. And it is understood that Above, the knowledge of evil does not cause harm, whereas man, from his lower aspect, is a "knower of good and evil," which causes sin and death (explained at length in *Torah Or*—by the author of the Tanya—s.v. *V'hanachash hayah arom*). Therefore, for Moshe, the "best man of the King," it did not cause harm that he knew that "I will be sanctified in My glory," as is known there, whereas for the "best man of the Queen" and his children, it was necessary to conceal this. And likewise, in this manner is the matter of the incident of the Golden Calf regarding Moshe and Yehoshua, and the decree of Haman regarding Mordechai and Esther. And the proof is that when they told Esther, she experienced a *niddah* flow—impure blood and nourishment for the *chitzonim*. — And this is similar to one whose mind is strong; bad news regarding the future, G-d forbid, will not disturb him from his affairs, whereas women, whose minds are light, are different. And Esther was protected from this knowledge, and there was no place for the nourishment of the *chitzonim* because she was occupied with the burning of *chametz* specifically, which is the nullification of evil entirely. And this is similar to the statement of our Sages (Pesachim 11a), "He himself searches for it to burn it; he eats from it."

May the Almighty protect each and every one within the entirety of Israel, and redeem us from being servants of Achashverosh, to be truly holy and to do what is good in His eyes with joy, in inwardness, and in completeness.
(From a letter of 17 Shevat, 5714)


## בא

## 232

### Bo

I received with pleasure the news regarding the continuation of your *talmud Torah* for the masses, and that these days you are completing *Maseches Pesachim*—a timely matter, thirty days before the *Chag*.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that this completion of the *Maseches* —which includes the blessing of the *Pesach*, the blessing of the *Zevach* in the *Mishnah*, the blessing of *Pidyon HaBen*, and the blessing of *Shehecheyanu* in the explanation of the *Mishnah*, which is the *Gemara*—be fitting.

The offering of the *Pesach* and its essence are dependent upon *milah*, which is a prerequisite for them; therefore, they are of the same category, as the *Mishnah* states at the beginning of *Maseches Kerisos*. Their inner essence is identical: the covenant (*bris*) between Hashem and Yisrael, which distinguishes them from the nations (*milah*) and redeems the children of Yisrael from exile (for all exiles are called *Mitzrayim*). And the concept of the *Zevach Shelamim*, which makes peace in the world [ftnref_1780_א], draws down spirituality into the physical; therefore, the meat is eaten by the *Kohanim* and also by the owners—eating in its literal sense.

From this, we can understand the explanation in the *Gemara* and the connection to *Pidyon HaBen*—analogous to the *Pesach* and *milah* mentioned above: the redemption of the firstborn sons of Yisrael, together with the blessing of *Shehecheyanu*, which we recite specifically over visible and revealed good [ftnref_1781_ב]. And the *halacha* is that the father of the son recites two blessings—He is our Father in Heaven.

May it be that in our immediate time, through *Mashiach Tzidkeinu*, He will redeem His firstborn son, Yisrael, from among the exiles, and we will say before Him a new song [ftnref_1782_ג]: "This is our G-d," as in the conclusion of *Maseches Taanis*, "Who has kept us alive and sustained us to this time..."

(From a letter dated 6 Adar, 5718)

Regarding what was written concerning the ruling of the Alter Rebbe in his *Shulchan Aruch*, *Orach Chaim* 453:14, that it suffices to have *shimur* (guarding) for the sake of the *mitzvah* in order to eat *matzah*, and not specifically [for the requirement of] "you shall eat *matzot* in the evening"—for according to this opinion, there is a *mitzvah* to eat *matzah* all seven days (and this is also stated in *Torah Sheleimah*, in the supplements to Vol. 11, in the commentary on *Shas Pesachim* 40a)—therefore, one cannot say this. For the opinion of the Alter Rebbe on this matter (ibid., end of section 475) is like the Rambam, that there is no *mitzvah* at all except for the first night. This is also implied by the simple wording of the Rosh and the *Tur Shulchan Aruch*, even though they are the proponents of the second opinion in 453:14, as noted there in the *Mareh Mekomos*. This is also implied by the Rambam, *Hilchos Chametz U’Matzah* 5:10 (see there in the *Mareh Mekomos* and in *Tzafnas Paneach* to the Rogatchover). Whether the definition of *lishmah* and the various opinions regarding eating *matzah* all seven days apply in general—this is discussed at length in *Torah Sheleimah* there. And this is not the place to elaborate.

(From a letter dated 28 Adar, 5720)

Regarding what was noted concerning the words of our Sages (*Bava Kamma* 98b) that everyone is commanded to remove *chametz* on *Pesach*, even though it is known that the obligation to remove *chametz* rests only upon the owner:

See the *Shulchan Aruch* of the Alter Rebbe, section 443, paragraph 7, that even though the liability for the *chametz* is not upon him, nevertheless he must remove it so that the owner of the *chametz* does not transgress "it shall not be seen," because all of Yisrael are responsible for one another, and they are not *metzuveh* (commanded) to allow a transgression...

(From a letter dated 28 Kislev, 5720)

It is brought in several books that participating in a *Pidyon HaBen* is equivalent to 84 fasts. This is discussed in the *Responsa Shem MiShimon*, First Edition, *Yoreh Deah* section 29 (its content: that this is a *tikkun* for the blemish of the *bris*, which requires 84 fasts). However, for the time being, I have not found a source for this in the books of Chabad Chassidus, and in any case, the aforementioned books are worthy to be relied upon.

(From a letter dated 22 MarCheshvan, 5715)


## יו"ד שבט

## 234

### 10 Shevat

I acknowledge receipt of your letter, in which you write about the *farbrengen* held during an *eis ratzon*. May it be the will of Hashem that these words of *hisorerus* achieve their intended effect, in accordance with the teaching of our Sages: "The study is not the main thing, but the *maaseh* (the deed)." This is especially pertinent as we have just emerged from the *yom hilula* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, our Nasi. Each year, his *aliyah* ascends higher and higher, even relative to the *aliyah* of the previous year. Consequently, those who are *mekushar*, who belong to him and follow his guidance, also ascend—*basar reisha azil* (the body follows the head)—though, of course, there must also be an *is'arusa d'lesata* (an awakening from below) and the actions of the lower realm. This is also understood from the *Maamar HaTikkunim* (as it appears in *Iggeret HaKodesh*; for the time being, I have found the entire matter in *Zohar Chadash*, 273a; see also there, 216b. In the *Tikkunim* (70:112a, 114a; 70:138a), I found only a portion of what is explained in *Iggeret HaKodesh* there—perhaps there is a copyist’s error in *Iggeret HaKodesh*, and a passage from *Tanya*, Chapter 44, regarding "the *Tikkunim*" was inadvertently inserted), which is cited in *Iggeret HaKodesh*, Epistle 27, like the sun shining from beneath the earth for six hundred thousand stars...
(From a letter dated 27 Shevat, 5718)

I was pleased to read in your letter of 12 Shevat the content of the discussions at the *farbrengen* during *re'eva d're'evin* (the time of greatest favor) and *leit zeifin* (when there is no anger, for the King is in a state of revelation). This is especially true on the *yom hilula* of the *Tzaddik Yesod Olam* who labored with *mesiras nefesh* on the line, "May Hashem add to me another son." As has been discussed previously, regarding the "delay" in producing a son, and regarding the "other" (*acher*), this also includes the most inferior category, regarding which it is proclaimed, "Except for *Acher*." Yet, even for him, the advice offered in our Torah—the Torah of life—is that he should push himself, and then he will enter. And one for whom miracles were performed (as our Sages state in *Berachos* 57a, "Yochanan, miracles were performed for him") can even dissipate the smoke.

There is another allusion to this, based on what is observed tangibly: as the rain and the material of the wood increase, the smoke also increases. Conversely, when the material is refined, and the rain itself becomes spiritual, there is no place for smoke, for it is already entirely spiritual and light.
*Yitzchak* (Isaac), who *meyached* (unifies) the Holy One, blessed be He, by placing His Name upon him (*Tanchuma, Toldos* 7), for his ashes (the most coarse element, the dust; *Iggeret HaKodesh*, Epistle 15) are also heaped upon the altar...
(From a letter dated 16 Shevat, 5717)

## 235

B"H, in the days between 10 and 15 Shevat, the New Year for Trees, 5747. Brooklyn, N.Y.
To the sons and daughters of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem grant them life,
Peace and blessing!

As we come from the day of 10 Shevat, the day of the *hilula* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, it is still "alive" in the memory of the concept of the eternity of the soul in general, and in particular the eternity of the soul of a *Nasi* in Israel. All his life in this world was bound up with and permeated by the eternity of Torah and *mitzvos*. This is especially so because the *baal hilula* established a generation, and generations of generations, of students and continuators who walk in his ways.

This is especially true since the primary goal of his *avodah* and activity was the dissemination of Torah (both the revealed and the inner dimensions) and *mitzvos* to the widest circles of Jews everywhere, until this reaches every Jew and the Jewish people as a whole—our youth and our elders, our sons and our daughters,

## 236

without exception. On the contrary: "All of us as one," and in the manner of "Stand ready, all of you," to say to Hashem: "We will do and we will hear"—all the *mitzvos* and the entire Torah, forever.

Therefore, the following double proposal and request is directed to each and every one, Jews wherever they may be, with this introduction:
Every year, and from year to year, on the day of the *hilula*, all the matters of the *baal hilula* must be—and indeed become—not merely continued, but primarily renewed with greater intensity and greater strength, as should be the case with all matters of goodness and holiness, in accordance with the instruction, "We ascend in holiness," especially regarding general and fundamental matters.

This renewal applies even to matters that existed previously, but which were not previously considered a "primary matter," or were not emphasized to the same degree as they are in their renewed state. Consequently, this renewal awakens in people in general, and in Jews in particular, fresh powers, which are expressed also in actual deed, for "the deed is the essential thing." Thus, these renewed matters (even if they are not new) become "as new," and even reach the level of a renewal that makes them "new" in the literal sense.

* * *

It is the nature of man, as created by the Holy One, blessed be He, that a daily phenomenon, or even a phenomenon that is not frequent but occurs alongside or within other matters—rather than as a primary matter—does not arouse special attention, even if the matter itself is as important as can be.

## 237

It is different when the matter appears as a primary matter, with appropriate added emphasis; then, the attitude toward it and the response to it are entirely different.
Regarding us—a matter that has already been spoken of in the past, but not with the full emphasis required when discussing a primary matter in daily life:
To make every Jewish home a "miniature sanctuary (*mikdash me'at*)," as is alluded to in the command and promise of the Holy One, blessed be He: "And they shall make Me a sanctuary, and I will dwell within them," as our Sages of blessed memory emphasize: it does not say "and I will dwell within *it*" (singular: in the sanctuary), but "within *them*" (plural)—within each and every one, in "your heart," "your soul," "your means/your money," in every Jewish home.

In simple words: we come to express with full emphasis that the matter of "and I will dwell within them" must be made a primary matter, and one must dedicate oneself to it in practice with the greatest effort, in thought, speech, and action, in order to bring this to practical realization in the fullest measure.

In greater clarity and detail: the "miniature sanctuary"—"and I will dwell within them"—in the heart of every Jew and in every Jewish home, will constitute a reflection and a mirror, as it were, of the general Sanctuary, which included within it, and served as a source for the entire world, all three pillars upon which the world stands: Torah, *avodah*, and acts of loving-kindness.
Torah—is emphasized in the first detail of "And they shall make Me a sanctuary"—in the command: "And they shall make an ark

## 242

in our land, because the verse will be fulfilled: "Show us Your kindness, Hashem, and grant us Your salvation" (Your kindness and Your salvation), and in the manner of "Show us," "And all flesh shall see"—with physical eyes, literally.

With respect and blessing,
And with a blessing of success in all that is mentioned,
[Signature]

* * *

B"H, in the days between 10 Shevat, the day of the *hilula* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, and 15 Shevat, the New Year for Trees, 5747. Brooklyn, N.Y.
To all the children of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem grant them life,
Peace and blessing!

In addition to the general and all-encompassing letter, there comes here, in particular, the double proposal and request to each of you, boy and girl, to make your room, your bed, your desk, etc.—a "home" of Torah, prayer, and acts of loving-kindness: to study Torah there every day, to say a prayer to Hashem, to give *tzedakah* in a *tzedakah* box (except on Shabbos and Yom Tov), and the like.
And each of you should have a *Siddur* (prayer book) of your own, a *Chumash* (or another book of Torah) of your own, and likewise, to distinguish, a *tzedakah* box of your own.
[And to write—on the page before the beginning of the *Siddur* or book—"The earth and its fullness belong to Hashem" (or the acronym "LaHashem Ha'aretz") and your name, as is the custom of Israel. And if possible—also on the *tzedakah* box.]

* * *

May the Holy One, blessed be He, bless and grant success to each of you to "grow," to mature, and to ascend in Torah, prayer, acts of loving-kindness, and *mitzvos*—in accordance with the allusion of the New Year for Trees, and to bring forth throughout the entire year many good fruits (good deeds),
—as per the many blessings of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe,
And may you do all this in good health and with joy.

With a blessing of great success in all this,
[Signature]

## 244

And in order to emphasize and highlight the special importance of the children's activity, the aforementioned request is presented in two letters:
Letter A, in length and detail—to the sons and daughters of Israel, for whom these matters are a fundamental obligation; and Letter B, in brevity and focus—to all the children of Israel, for whom these matters are a matter of education.
But we are promised, "Educate a child according to his way, (so that) even when he grows old, he will not depart from it."
This increases with greater intensity and greater strength the merit of the educators, and also their responsibility—since it touches upon the entire duration of the life of the one being educated.

My request is twofold—as stated—that parents, teachers, and guides, etc., should awaken and influence the children in all the above.
Furthermore, and this too is essential—that they explain to the children what is explained and clarified in the books of our early sages, the great ones of Israel (from where the content of the long letter was condensed and copied, the point of which is)—that the general Holy Temple includes the three things upon which the world stands: Torah, prayer, and acts of loving-kindness, and something similar must be in the home and the four cubits of each and every Jew, "from young to old, children and women."
They will certainly find the style and the language appropriate to the level of the children's intellect, understanding, and age.
It is worthwhile that the guides should ask the children: Are they using their *Siddur*, *Chumash*, and *tzedakah* box—from time to time, and especially on auspicious days?

* * *

This double request will surely be publicized everywhere, and especially among those who have significant influence in the matter of education.
My hope is strong that the words will be accepted and will achieve their effect.
They will certainly succeed in all this with great and abundant success—as we see tangibly in the recent period the measure of success in these activities, and it will certainly be so in the future as well.
As the Holy One, blessed be He, who is the One who commands, said: "And they shall make Me a sanctuary, and I will dwell within them" (as explained in the general letter, the interpretation of our Sages of blessed memory regarding the precision of "within *them*"): "And test Me now with this!"
And furthermore, and this too is essential—that through this, one merits to hasten and advance the building of the general, and primary, Holy Temple, the Third Holy Temple, which will be built speedily in our days, literally.

## 245

The year of the passing of our Nasi, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, has ended.
The longing intensifies, for "the summer has ended, the winter is passing, and we have not been saved."
But on the other hand, habit takes its toll. There is room for concern that the matter will become "old," and the light and warmth of the connection to our Nasi, to his Torah, and to his instructions—which are all one—will go on decreasing, Heaven forbid.
These are the words that Moshe spoke regarding the Torah: "These words that I command you this day." Its interpretation: like a new royal decree (*diotagma*) that everyone runs toward.
And regarding the *mitzvos*: "My *mitzvos* that I command you this day." Its interpretation: that they should be new to you as if you heard them on that very day.
(From a letter dated 15 Shevat, New Year for Trees, 5711)


## בשלח 

## 245

### Beshalach

In response to your letter from the beginning of the month of Adar, in which you express your bewilderment regarding the explanation of the splitting of the Yam Suf brought in the Sefer Baal Shem Tov on Parshas Behaaloscha in the name of the Baal Shem Tov—that it was as if it were natural, and the miracle was that Hashem, at the beginning of Creation, embedded in nature that on a certain day the sea would split—this is unlike what is explained in many places, that the splitting of the Yam Suf was a miracle, and a very great miracle at that.

Regarding this, the aforementioned book is a compilation from various sources, and it requires study as to how accurate the statements are in the books from which it was compiled. For in matters such as these, an inaccuracy of even a few words can change the intent from one extreme to the other. This is especially true given the well-known fact that the Baal Shem Tov would speak words of Torah in the vernacular (*le'az*) and not in Lashon HaKodesh, and the transcriber did not always capture the Baal Shem Tov’s intent, even when the compiler was present at that time and place. See an example of this in Iggeres HaKodesh by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, section 26 (141a).

It is highly probable that this is the case here as well, for you are correct in your observation that the splitting of the Yam Suf is considered a very great miracle. See also Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, chapter 2.

As for the substance of the matter, even if we were to assume that someone did say something regarding the splitting of the Yam Suf in the style quoted in the name of the Baal Shem Tov as mentioned above, it is known that in such instances, one often answers "according to your approach and your logic"—*afilu etimmar* (even if we were to say), meaning: even if we were to say (though the matter is not so) that there was a natural element involved—nevertheless, etc., as is explained there.

It should be noted that many of the great scholars and researchers of Israel in past generations explained the matter of the rainbow in this way—about which it is said that it is a "sign of the covenant"—even though it is explained that it is a natural phenomenon. See the commentaries on the Torah, Parshas Noach.

One may also interpret the aforementioned style according to what is written in Rabbeinu Bachya (Beshalach 14:27): "It was placed in the nature of the water, etc." See there.

(From a letter dated 4 Adar, 5719)

---

...Regarding what is written in Targum Yonasan, Shemos 14:21, that engraved upon the staff were, etc., and "six mothers and from the city," for it is standard in all places to mention the four mothers (Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah), and they are not called "fathers and mothers" unless, etc..

One can say simply that the staff mentioned not specifically the Patriarchs, but rather every single tribe, and therefore they added the mother of each one as well...

(From a letter dated 7 Shevat, 5720)

---

...And may it be Hashem’s will that regarding the language of the Parsha that we read this past Shabbos, "I will bring healing to you," as explained in the *Roshei Teivos* of "For I am Hashem your healer" (*Ki Ani Hashem Rofecha*): *Ari"ch*—for all healing comes from above (*ari"ch*). (See Zohar Vol. 3, 292b; Maor V'Shemesh, entry *Arich*; Koheles Yaakov, entry *Arucha*; and see also Zohar Chadash Vol. 3, 204a; 205b; Zohar Chadash, Balak 54c)...

(From a letter dated 14 Shevat, 5715)

---

...And may it be His will that from here on, you shall be heralded only with good, in a revealed and manifest way. And regarding matters of health, may it be specifically in the manner of the healing of the Ribono shel Olam, as it is written, "For I am Hashem your healer," and consequently, "I will not place upon you [the diseases that I placed upon Egypt]"—for it is known that [the word *Rofecha*] is an acronym for *Arich*. Regarding this it is said, "Your healing shall quickly sprout," [which is] the good almonds, more than any almond of Aharon the High Priest...

(From a letter dated 9 Tammuz, 5717)

---

...Regarding what was written about the Shabbos meals—that there appear to be contradictions in the statements of the Zohar.

The order is as stated by Rashbi (Zohar Vol. 3, 88b), and as we say in *Atkinu Se'udata*: *Chakal Tapuchin Kadishin* [Field of Holy Apples] is *Ze'er Anpin*. As for what is written in Zohar Vol. 3 (88a)—"the first meal corresponds to the Holy Ancient One, etc., the second meal corresponds to the Holy Field of Apples, etc."—this has already been explained in *Or HaChama* there, that it is explaining according to the order of the verses and not according to the order of the meals. Likewise, what is written in Zohar Vol. 3, 288b, is according to the order of the excellence of the *Midos*—as is written in *Or HaChama* to Zohar Vol. 3, 88b. And in the notes of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe on the *Drushei Se'udos Shabbos*, the matter is explained according to Chassidus...

(From a letter dated 20 Nissan, 5717)

---

...Regarding what you wrote about the caution not to make Kiddush before 6:00 or 7:00 in the evening on Shabbos, the intent is understood to be an hour consisting of sixty minutes, for the movement of the constellations is the same in summer and winter, and even at midday there is no difference between locations in the south and the north. Consequently, the "sixth hour" means six equal hours after midday.

As for what you wrote, that this is not a concern in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established), and similarly regarding *netilas yadayim* before a meal, surely you will inform me of the reasoning of those who are not concerned about this in Eretz Yisrael, and whether they are reliable authorities...

(From a letter dated 18 Teves, 5716)

---

...Regarding what is written in *Toras Chayim*, beginning of Parshas Lech Lecha, page 96, top of column 2, that even the eating of Shabbos "materializes" the body due to the physical pleasure in the body which is not refined and is mixed with absolute good and evil from the Tree of Knowledge of Good and Evil—which seemingly does not align with what is written in *Toras Chayim*, Parshas Vayakhel, pages 627 and 647, that the eating of Shabbos does not materialize, for "your Shabbos" is not mentioned [as being materialized].

The explanation for this is that although the term "materialize" is used in both places, the difference is that there is no evil in the eating of Shabbos, but it does "materialize" in the sense of what is permitted, and this is possible even in the eating of Shabbos. This is all the more so and *kal v'chomer* from what is written in *Toras Chayim*, Parshas Lech Lecha mentioned above, that even the love of the *Nefesh HaBahamis* that comes in a felt way is derived from this, etc. See there.

Incidentally, these matters are discussed in *Torah Or*, beginning of Parshas Chayei Sarah, and in the *Siddur*, *Seder Se'udas Shabbos* (second meal, *d'h* *Yigaleh Lan Ta'amei*), and likewise in *Derech Mitzvosecha*, page 179 and there. See there...

(From a letter dated 7 Teves, 5714)

---

## 248

I was alarmed to receive your letter regarding the fast on Shabbos—a *yahrzeit* fast. There are several opinions on this, but according to all, one does not fast. In my opinion, it is better to move it to Friday, and if that is impossible, one delays it to Sunday, or one does not fast at all. See the opinions on this in *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim* 568, section 9. And in the *Acharonim* there: *Turei Zahav*, section 429, subsection 3; and in the *Shulchan Aruch* of our Rebbe there, section 9; and in the books cited in *Sdei Chemed*, *Asifat Dinim*, *Ma'areches Aveilus*, subsection 96; and in the book *Kol Bo* by Rabbi Grunwald, page 390. In my opinion, even *hataras nedarim* (annulment of vows) is not applicable here. In any case, do not fast on Shabbos.

(From a letter dated 26 Teves, 5714)


## תיקון עירובין

## 248

### Fixing Eiruvin

... *See*. *Section 2.* The opinion of Rashi. This is cited many times by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe in his Shulchan Aruch, *Orach Chaim* 345:11, and in many other places. In the responsa *Beis Av*, Vol. 2, Section 5, the author lists thirty Rishonim who hold like Rashi.

*Ibid.* *Section 1.* The reason for the number of 600,000 — that non-Jews are also included — can be explained by the fact that they were commanded regarding Shabbos at Marah (see *Tosafos* s.v. *Atchumin*, *Shabbos* 87b), and at that time they still had the status of Bnei Noach (as is known to be the opinion of several Rishonim on this). Even afterwards, at the Giving of the Torah, the laws of Shabbos were defined "as He commanded you" at Marah.

*Page 2.* *Section 3.* According to all opinions, a *reshus harabim* is defined by Torah law. This requires further study and clarification, for it seems to me that all the streets eventually end at bridges and tunnels that are blocked by *tzuras hapesach* or by partitions and "shranken" (barriers) used for collecting tolls and the like. — *See* the *Ateres Zekeinim* of the Rav of Buchach, *Orach Chaim* 345.

*Page 3.* The definition of a sea or river. (This has practical implications for the writing of a *get* and the like.) Seemingly, one could say it depends on whether the waters are stagnant and remain in their place (even if there are waves), or if they are flowing (*Mikvaos* 5:4; *Makkos* 4a; *Yevamos* 121a; and elsewhere. See also the responsa *Tzafnas Paneach* by the Rogatchover Gaon, sections 58-59). But in truth, it seems to me that in every instance it is according to its specific nature. In the laws of *eiruvin*, it depends on what one actually sees—whether (at least at times) it forms a sandbar and solidifies. *See there.* — This explains why the Rishonim and Acharonim detail various laws and distinctions regarding these concerns in different rivers, in *ukim*, etc.—even though they are not explicitly explained in the *Shas*.

Based on this, one must clarify all parts of the perimeter of Manhattan brought here. — *See* the books cited in this regard in *Orchos Chaim* (the new edition), *Orach Chaim* 343.

*Page 3.* The concern that perhaps the sea might form a sandbar, according to one line of reasoning. This requires further study, as the Rema rules this way (see *Yad Malachi*, *Klalei HaRema* 18). The Alter Rebbe copied this into his halachic ruling in *Orach Chaim* 363:35.

*Ibid.* The opinion of the *Chasam Sofer*. The opinion of the Alter Rebbe (*ibid.*) is that it is proper to be concerned for the words of the one who forbids it.

## 249

*Page 4.* *Section 8.* That it is possible to see from the top of tall buildings, etc. — It does not seem correct to me at all to say that by building a tower whose top reaches the heavens in the middle of a very large area, the entire area is transformed from a *reshus harabim* by Torah law into a *reshus hayachid*. One cannot say that any area from which the perimeter can be seen via a building or the like is a *reshus hayachid* by Torah law; if so, the question of the *Shas*—that the entire world is surrounded by the ocean (*Eiruvin* 22b, according to the explanation brought in the *Kuntres* that the perimeter must be visible)—remains in its place, as is recounted regarding Solomon (*Yerushalmi*, cited in *Tosafos* s.v. *Kekadur*, *Avodah Zarah* 41a).

Therefore, one must say that according to the above, it must be visible while standing on the surface of the earth. In *Bechoros* (54b), it says it is sixteen *mil*. Perhaps in the case at hand it is more than that, for there it requires that the eye have dominion to guard and count, which is not the case with the perimeter of partitions.

— And to note regarding the above, from *Pesachim* (94a): "One can enter with horses and mules, etc." Also see regarding the measurement of a "nearby place" (*Moed Katan* 22a), in our days when people travel by train, airplane, and the like—the discussion on this in the books cited in *Sefer Kol Bo*—by Rabbi Grunwald, Vol. 1, p. 350.

*Page 5.* *End of Section 11.* Further study is needed in the *Shulchan Aruch* of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, *Orach Chaim* 349:42.

*Ibid.* *Section 12.* *See* the *Biur Halacha* of the author of the *Mishnah Berurah*, *Orach Chaim* 358:9.

*Ibid.* *Section 3.* It is a subject of dispute—see the books cited in the glosses of the *Maharsham* in *Orchos Chaim* (the new edition), *Orach Chaim* 358.

* * *

Regarding the matter that it is a *mitzvah* to fix *eiruvin*—see *Eiruvin* 28a; *Tur Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim* 366:13; *Shitah Mekubetzes* to *Beitzah* (16b); Responsa of the *Rosh*, *Klal* 21; *Rashbatz* (Vol. 2, 37); *Chasam Sofer*, *Orach Chaim* 99; Responsa *Beis Av*, Vol. 2, Section 1.

It is worth noting that the entire latter book discusses matters of *eiruvin*, and there is a discussion there on many of the details brought in this *Kuntres*.

(From a letter, 15 Iyar, 5714)

[New Section]

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from 1 Kislev, along with the *Kuntres* regarding the possibilities and necessity of fixing an *eiruv* in Manhattan.

There is already a *Kuntres* on this, "Proposal for Fixing an Eiruv," by the esteemed Rabbi Zvi Eisenstadt, which is worked out in detail with citations, etc., in what you wrote, and more, with additions to it.

It is surprising that you did not mention in all the discussions in the *Kuntres* you sent me the matter of the "seeds" (grain) found in the city, which according to many Rishonim and Acharonim nullify the partitions. Likewise, you did not touch upon the fact that

## 250

part of Manhattan is surrounded by the sea, and even the part called the "river" is a major question as to whether it falls under the category of a river according to *halacha*; I will not elaborate here. See the *Kuntres* by Rabbi Eisenstadt mentioned above. Likewise, *Mikvaos* 5:4, *Makkos* 4a, and elsewhere. Responsa *Tzafnas Paneach* by the Rogatchover Gaon, sections 58-59, regarding the definition of a river according to law. Likewise, as explained in the aforementioned *Kuntres*, there are many places that were not enclosed, in addition to the issue that parts of the partitions were not enclosed for residential purposes.

Regarding what you noted concerning the dispute among the Rishonim whether it requires 600,000 people passing through: this is how our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe ruled in his *Shulchan Aruch*, Section 345, Paragraph 11. See the responsa *Beis Av*, Vol. 2, Section 5, where he counts thirty opinions from the Rishonim who hold this way.

Regarding what you noted about what the Rav of Buchach wrote—that there is no proof that non-Jews are not included in the 600,000—in many places among the Acharonim it is implied that non-Jews are indeed included in the 600,000. The basis for this is that they were commanded regarding Shabbos at Marah (see *Tosafos* s.v. *Atchumin*, *Shabbos* 87b), and at that time they still had the status of Bnei Noach (as is known to be the opinion of most Rishonim on this). Even afterwards, at the Giving of the Torah, the laws of Shabbos were defined "as He commanded you" (at Marah).

Regarding what you wrote about the matter that it is a *mitzvah* to fix *eiruvin*, see, in addition to what you mentioned in your letter, *Shitah Mekubetzes* to *Beitzah* 16b, Responsa of the *Rosh*, *Klal* 21, *Tashbetz* Vol. 2, Section 37, *Chasam Sofer*, *Orach Chaim* 99, Responsa *Beis Av*, Vol. 2, Section 1.

(From a letter, 4 Tammuz, 5714)

---

[New Section]

I acknowledge receipt of your letter in response to the comments I wrote regarding matters of *eiruvin*.

Regarding what you wrote about the "seeds" (grain), that you did not see seeds in Manhattan, it is surprising, for they are numerous in many places there.

Likewise, regarding what you wrote about the formation of a sandbar: in a place where the prohibition is only rabbinic, we are not concerned that a sandbar might form. Therefore, it must be that this opinion was not accepted, since according to many Rishonim and many Acharonim, for practical *halacha*, there is no *reshus harabim* in these times, yet they still bring and discuss at length the concern that a sandbar might form even now.

Regarding what you wrote about my comment that Shabbos is different because they were commanded at Marah, and you raise a difficulty from *Tosafos Shabbos* 87b s.v. *Atchumin*—it seems clear to me that I also pointed to this *Tosafos* in my letter, for there it is implied

## 251

that according to one opinion, they were commanded regarding *hotza'ah* (carrying) at Marah, and from that we learn also for the other, since that is not where their dispute lies. And what you want to compare this to—circumcision (and note the *Peirush HaMishnayos* at the end of Chapter 2 of *Chullin*)—I already hinted at this in my letter, where I noted that regarding Shabbos, at Sinai it was said to them "as He commanded you" at Marah, which is not the case with circumcision, as is understood.

(From a letter, 18 Elul, 5714)

---

[New Section]

I acknowledge receipt of your letter along with the "Kuntres Fixing Eiruvin" by your esteemed self, and the *Kuntres* is returned herewith.

Regarding what you wrote about an *haskamah* (approbation)—it is known that this is not the custom of the House of the Rebbe. We follow the custom of our ancestors. Especially since the time does not at all permit studying the book as is required. Furthermore—and this is the main point for me—in every place, "I am in the place of the Rav," who is my grandfather, our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, author of the *Tanya* and the *Shulchan Aruch*, and we follow specifically the Rav. In this, of course, is included what he wrote in his *Shulchan Aruch* (363:35) that the sea does not rise to serve as a partition.

Regarding what you want to force and interpret this ruling—that it applies only if there is a concern that the garbage will also be removed and only one partition will remain—with all due respect, there is no place for this at all, for he explicitly wrote his ruling in the *Shulchan Aruch* there—regarding public garbage that is not intended to be cleared away. And when the sea forms a sandbar, two partitions will remain adjacent to each other like a door, and a *lechi* or *korah* on the third side.

* * *

Now, although, despite the above, I was happy to read at the end of the *Kuntres* that "the reward of the worker is his hire, etc."

(Although surely without a blessing, and not as the superficial reading of the language implies, for one has not emerged from the many doubts. And blessings are not an impediment.)

In my opinion, it is a great and wonderful merit for you, even if you were to say that according to several opinions there is room to discuss several details and doubts,

nevertheless, it is clear in my absolute and firm opinion—that one should not print, nor publish in any other way, that the matter has been completed and the *eiruv* has been fixed (at least according to your opinion).

Regarding what you wrote at the end of the *Kuntres* about the benefit of publication—in order to save even those who intend to violate the law, as in the *Shas* (*Nazir* 23a),

surely you also estimate how many of these willful sinners—study or even just know about such books and *Kuntresim*.

This is not the case regarding those who are observant of Torah and *mitzvos*, of whom the Sages said that they "permit themselves"

## 252

(if they can only find some basis or pretext) and that the publication of the matter is liable to lead them to breaches, etc. And after the publication, the matter will be in the category of "that which is crooked cannot be made straight," even if one wanted to.

— The great warning at the beginning of the *Kuntres*—we have already seen tangibly that it does not help in a printed and published matter, since, unfortunately, the method is prevalent that "if it is permitted, it is comfortable." Especially in this country, where the "Rabbis" stand at their post—a post against Hashem and against His Torah—to breach the wall of religion and Judaism.

May it be the will that in his days and in our days, the statement of our Sages will be fulfilled in practice (*Yerushalmi Taanis* 1:1): "If Israel would keep one Shabbos as it should be kept, immediately the son of David would come."

— In the *Bavli* (*Shabbos* 118b) it says "two Shabbosos according to their law." This does not contradict the statement in the *Yerushalmi Taanis* mentioned above, as our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe explained in his book *Likutei Torah*, *Parshas Behar*, in the *Maamar* "Es Shabbosotai Tishmoru." See there. —

And with the addition in *Shemos Rabbah* (end of Chapter 28): Why? Because it is weighed against all the *mitzvos*...

(From a letter, Rosh Chodesh Adar, 5718)


## ט"ו בשבט

### Tu B'Shvat
