## יתרו

## 253

### Yisro

... Incidentally, to write regarding the content discussed here during the farbrengen : the idea that the revelation at the time of Matan Torah was merely an "addition" is inherently absurd. Matan Torah is the totality of the order of the entire Seder Hishtalshelus, and so on. There is no need to elaborate on something so simple. What was discussed, however, was that although ten [people] constitute a *parheisya* (public assembly) that fills this entire world—meaning it fills it in terms of breadth—it is different regarding depth and height. An *himshech* (drawing down) from a place that is most lofty involves many levels that are even far above the level of ten. It is a simple fact that these levels are infinite in height and depth. This is the concept of *s'rivo* (sixty myriads)—the *chacham harazim* (wise one of the mysteries) who draws down from the level of *raz* (mystery). And similarly regarding Matan Torah. It seems that several matters are being recorded—something like this—and it is astonishing that the reader does not sense this at all, which indicates a total lack of attentiveness. *V'dai l'meivin* (and a word to the wise is sufficient).

(From a letter, 22 Elul, 5720)

---

... Regarding your question about the difficulty you have in explaining to them the matter of the mitzvos—whether they are observed due to *kabbalas ol* (acceptance of the yoke) or whether they have a rationale in the intellect: the general point here is that the mitzvos were given by Hashem to human beings. Consequently, it is understood that the wisdom within them is limitless. On the other hand, it is also understood that there is some grasp and hold for human intellect, and this is the subject of the *taamei hamitzvos* (reasons for the mitzvos) brought in the sefarim. But since they originate from the wisdom and will of the Ribono shel Olam, it is simple that no matter how much a person delves into the reasons for the mitzvos and their benefits, it is never complete. For it is impossible for a limited being to grasp and encompass a limitless matter; one can only grasp the "fringe of its edge" and a mere fraction of it.

Furthermore, since the mitzvos were given by the Creator, Yisbarach, for the benefit of the human being created by Him, it is certain that He, Yisbarach, is capable of intending the good of the creature He created. Just as it is impossible for a person to say they will not eat until they understand with their intellect the benefit of eating and drinking—and just as it is absurd for a person who is ill in their head to say they will not accept any medicine until they understand with their intellect if it will help them—on the contrary, taking the ingredients, medicines, and eating and drinking strengthens the brain and the power of the intellect, so that in time they will be able to understand the benefit of eating, drinking, and the medicines.

The matter is the same regarding the mitzvos. It is certain that they can be understood, at least to the "fringe of their edge," even by human intellect. But this is not a condition, *chas v'shalom*, for the fulfillment of mitzvos and the study of Torah. On the contrary, the *Torah u'mitzvos* are the very things that lead to a state where, in time, one's intellect will be qualified to understand and attain the aforementioned.

## 254

One could elaborate on this, but the explanation must be appropriate to the level of the students. I rely on your understanding that you will be able to adapt the matters to their power of comprehension and attainment.

Enclosed are some points from what I have said here in English, which you can use to understand the aforementioned point. May Hashem grant you success in your *avodah b'kodesh*, as well as success in your personal matters, and proper health for your wife and daughter, *shichyu*.

(From a letter, 1 Shevat, 5712)

... To write to him that there is a question that is troubling him, for which he has not yet found an answer, and he is suffering from the doubt, etc., and he asks for references and citations where he might find the answer to his question.

The question is: what is the source that the fulfillment of mitzvos is required of us even in a standing and situation where the matter is connected to difficulties and toil, even to the point of a *nisayon* (test)?

It is astonishing that there is doubt and a question regarding such a simple matter. I will explain my thoughts: this doubt could only have a place in one of two scenarios: 1) If the One who commanded the mitzvah commanded it in an unrefined manner—meaning, He only gave the main points and the details are missing, so that there is room for many doubts regarding those matters that were not specified. 2) If the One who commanded the mitzvah could not foresee every possible standing and situation in which the one commanded would find himself, and consequently, it is impossible to know if one is commanded to fulfill the command in this standing and situation as well.

Since the foundation of our faith (incidentally, this is also the foundation of other faiths, *l'havdil*) is that the One who commanded the mitzvah is the ultimate perfection, and this is therefore evident even in the commands that were given in a clarified manner; and furthermore, He is the One who knows the future, and in the perfection of His wisdom, He foresaw every possible standing and situation in which the recipient of the command would be found in the present and in the future—the near future and even the distant future—then the two aforementioned conditions certainly do not exist. Therefore, one must find in the Torah of the One who commanded the mitzvah the manner and requirement for the fulfillment of the mitzvah, which generally has no limitation, except for one limitation: "And he shall live by them," etc. As explained by our Sages in many places (among them Yoma 85b), from this we learn that only *pikuach nefesh* (saving a life) overrides the matters of the Torah, and nothing else. Similarly, the other limitations that exist in mitzvos, such as *hiddur mitzvah* (beautifying a mitzvah) up to a third, are also explicitly explained in the Torah of the One who commanded the mitzvah, in such a way that there is no room for any doubt. And with this, his doubt is also negated.

(From a letter, 27 Nissan, 5720)

## 255

... 1) Regarding his note that concerning the *taamim* (cantillation marks) in the Torah—whether it is correct to read the verses according to the *peshat* (literal meaning) of the Scripture, or according to the *taamim*—there was no doubt in his mind, and the general doubt is only regarding one specific case. And it is precisely in this that the doubt lies, because according to the rules of the *taamim* in Scripture, the *taamim* in these verses should have been in a different manner than they are in actuality, because one rule is overridden by another rule.

Answer: The rules of the *taamim*, as I wrote to him in the previous letter, are for the most part merely the work of human hands, who summarized them by searching through the *taamim* in the Scriptures. In order to resolve the contradictions that exist from place to place, they derived these rules. Consequently, if another person were to take an interest in this and could find a rule that would resolve all the difficulties in a different way, then it is possible that the previous rule would be nullified, and they would hold by the rule that this person invents (of course, this is only regarding most of the rules of the *taamim*, for some of them are founded on "holy mountains," and as is known, there are some rules of grammar and music that are founded on the wisdom of Kabbalah). This is unlike the *Torah Shebe'al Peh*, which was entrusted to the discretion of the Sages of the Torah.

The conclusion from the above is that even in the specific case he raised, in my opinion, it is clear that one must read it according to the *taamim*.

2) More than all of the above: even if the aforementioned rules were received as *Halacha L'Moshe MiSinai*, since the detail that a certain rule is overridden by another rule is also *Halacha L'Moshe MiSinai*—that in this specific place the *taamim* must be according to the second rule—then one must also chant the Scripture in such a manner. As I suggested in the previous letter from the Zohar, the *taamim* were given to chant the Scriptures with them, and they are like the soul and spirit to the body.

3) A supporting point to the above: In other places, it is explicit that they should chant differently than the written text (in *pashṭa zarqa tevir qadma*, which are always at the end of a word; in *tevir*, which is always at the beginning of a word; see also Shemini 10:2), which implies that there is no other way.

4) His question as to why one rule is stronger than another, such that it is overridden and not the other way around: as mentioned above, the rules were founded on the basis of the reality that they saw in the Scriptures, and this compelled the grammarians and the masters of the *taamim* to include a rule that in a case where two rules contradict each other, we see in the Scripture which of them is superior and overrides the other. The reason for the overriding, simply put, could be that it depends on the beauty of the melody and the pleasantness of the voice.

5) Regarding what he wrote as to why I did not mention the *sugya* in Nedarim that speaks about the *taamim*: the answer to this is in the letter where I cited the sefarim brought in *Pekuos Sadeh*, in which the *sugya* of Nedarim is also explained as much as is necessary.

(From a letter, 8 Kislev, 5712)

## 256

... And regarding the matter of *tzedakah*, our Sages said that "the one who causes [others] to do is greater than the one who does," which is even more than the saying of our Sages, "the wine belongs to the master, but the thanks go to the one who pours."

Incidentally, the well-known question is: since they say "the wine belongs to the master, but the thanks go to the one who pours," then why is *avodah zarah* (idol worship) forbidden, since through them, too, the *shefa* (bounty) is drawn down below, as it is written, "and with the bounty of the crops of the sun and the bounty of the yield of the moons"? The answer is simple: the sun, the moon, and all the host of heaven do not possess free will; they are merely like an axe in the hand of the woodcutter, where there is no place to give thanks to the axe. This is not the case if the one who pours is a possessor of free will, for then, by his own good will, he becomes an agent to bring the good into actual reality, and therefore he is deserving of thanks. It follows from this also that since the *malachim* (angels) do not possess free will, as brought in Tanya, Chapter 39, at the beginning, and even among the creatures below, free will is found only in the Jewish people, the matter of "thanks to the one who pours" is not truly applicable except to the Jewish people.

And it is understood that free will in its entirety belongs only to the Creator Himself, for there is no thing that compels Him, *chas v'shalom*, and therefore His will is free. This is not the case with all created beings, for it is impossible for them to be completely free, since, in the end, their nature, their intellect, or their will and desire compel them to perform this action and not its opposite. And even if the compulsion comes from within, then even in that case, the choice is not free. And since free will is applicable only to the Essence and Being of the *Ein Sof*, *Baruch Hu*, who is the ultimate perfection, then even below, there is no place for this except in the human being who is made "in Our image, after Our likeness," for you specifically are called "man."

(From a letter, 6 Tammuz, 5711)

In response to your letter from the 22nd (and it is a great wonder regarding a yeshiva *avreich* from the lineage of *Anash* and *Temimim* that in his letter he indicates the date by their numbering, at the same time that on that very day he said, "Today is the fifth day of the week," based on the command, "Remember the Shabbos day to keep it holy," and furthermore, it is during the days of *Hagbalah* before Matan Torah)...

(From a letter, 9 Sivan, 5718)

## 257

... An old, empty pot on the fire—it is a wonder what *tikkun* (rectification) there is in this, as it is destructive, especially regarding metal. And it is visible to the senses, and it is a full verse regarding calamity (Yechezkel 24:11): "And set it empty upon the coals thereof, that the brass of it may be hot," etc. And what is written regarding this in *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim*, Section 318, Paragraph 12—there, water is inside it. (And if in such a manner they permitted it, how much more so that one should not forbid it when it is empty, as it is destructive, lest he intend to begin the work of refining!) Therefore, all the *poskim* in Section 253, Paragraph 3, ruled simply: "An old, empty pot," and they did not distinguish between earthenware and metal. (And from what is written at the end of Section 502 regarding earthenware, one could say that, on the contrary, metal is more lenient, and there is room to permit it even when it is new. See there.)

(From a letter, 21 Shevat, 5715)


## הלכות שבת

## 257

### Hilchos Shabbos

...Regarding the matter of sewing, I believe I at least hinted at this in my previous letter. Seemingly, the concept of sewing consists of two details: a) Connecting two separate items by means of a third element. b) That the connecting element must be applied by means of a sewing thread—meaning, it enters the perforation with difficulty, etc. A connection can also be made by means of a metal wire, just as one of the threads in the Mishkan was made of gold (and with this, his doubt regarding an iron wire, as mentioned in his letter, is resolved). Therefore, one who joins papers or leathers by means of a third element—glue—is also liable.

With this, we can also understand the distinction between the concept of "joining parts" (chibur perakim) and "sewing" (tofer). Sewing is done by means of a third element, whereas the concept of joining parts is not. This is also the basis for the permissibility when the perforations are wide, fixed, and round, because then the thread does not enter with difficulty. According to the above, we can also understand the permissibility, which is cited as a simple matter, of inserting hooks into loops. This is not comparable to what he brought in his letter from the *Korban Nesanel* regarding the prohibition of connecting a garment with a pin (*shpilke*), as that does not possess the conditions for permissibility mentioned above.

According to the above, we can also understand the permissibility of a zipper, since in this case there is no third element that connects them. It falls under the law of a "vessel of parts" (keli shel perakim); a vessel that has grooves is permitted to be assembled on Shabbos, since it is not the work of an artisan (*ma'aseh uman*) and since it is made to be opened and closed constantly (see *Taz* and *Magen Avraham*, Siman 313, Se'if 6, and in the *Shulchan Aruch* of our Rebbe, there, Se'if 21). Furthermore, even if there were a connecting thread in the case of a zipper, according to the above, it should be permitted, as it is similar to a round, sewn, and wide perforation through which one is permitted to insert laces. The reason for this is that it is not like sewing, which is tight. And although a zipper is also tight, it is understood that the tightening of metal against metal is not comparable to fabric against fabric, similar to what is brought regarding *chatzitzah* (interposition) in *tevilah* (*Shabbos* 57a). And let us not add to this.

Note: 1) According to the above, we can also understand why one tightens a shoe by means of a shoelace that enters the perforations on both sides of the shoe; it is similar to the aforementioned laces, and this is done even if the metal ring surrounding the perforation is missing, and no one raises an objection or doubts this. 2) Regarding what was mentioned above concerning the permissibility of inserting hooks into loops:

## 258

Seemingly, this refers to hooks sewn on one side of the garment and loops sewn on the other. This is not like the hooks and loops on the curtains of the Mishkan, where the hooks were a separate item; according to the above, that would be a *toldah* (derivative) of sewing...
(From a letter dated 27 Shevat, 5713)

In response to your letter, and the enclosed discussion regarding the use of a safety pin (*zicher nadel*) on Shabbos:
It is understandable that I was alarmed by the conclusion of your response, that it is not only forbidden but that you even fear a Torah prohibition, Heaven forbid. Far be it from the seed of my father-in-law to cause so many of the kosher daughters of Israel in our generation and in the generations before us to be considered as having erred in such matters. Who is greater than the *Korban Nesanel* (*Shabbos*, Perek 7, sub-section 6, which your honor cites in your response), who was careful even not to forbid it explicitly, but only wrote that he was surprised at how the world follows this custom, etc. It is understood that just as the Mishnah says that it is a mitzvah to uphold the words of the Sages, it is a mitzvah to uphold the custom of the elderly women of Israel from many generations without anyone protesting against them.

Regarding the reasons for the permissibility, we can say several things, and it is worthwhile to combine them to explain the aforementioned custom:
a) With metal and a metal wire, there is no "sewing." Although there is no explicit proof for this, there is a mnemonic for it in that we learn all the *melachos* of Shabbos from the Mishkan. Even though there was also a gold thread in the weaving, it is obvious that they did not sew with these threads, for such a surprising matter would have required an explicit command. From what is stated in *Menachos* 41a, which mentions *sichi*—which according to the *Aruch* means pegs—it is understood that there must be a matter of connection, and it does not matter at all in what manner, whether by sewing or in another way. It is also simple that even regarding *kilayim*, the Torah does not mention "sewing," but rather "together." Consequently, there is no proof from there for liability for sewing on Shabbos. And what is found in some things as a connection or sewing not by means of threads is specifically in a matter where it is the way to connect it in such a manner. It is simple in every place that liability for *melachah* on Shabbos exists only when the *melachah* is performed in its usual manner, not in an unusual way (*shinui*), unlike *kilayim*.

Regarding what your honor wrote in your response, that Shabbos and *kilayim* are equal—to me, it is impossible to say such a thing, as mentioned above. The proof is already known from *Shabbos* 48, beginning of side b: "This is a connection, and this is not a connection"—see there.
b) It is already known the opinion of Rabbeinu Yoel, which is the accepted *halachah* (*Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim*, Siman 317, Se'if 3), that there must be a "permanent sewing" (*tefirah shel kayama*). "Permanent" in the context of Shabbos is explicitly defined in the context of a "permanent knot" (*kesher shel kayama*). See the *Shulchan Aruch* of our Rebbe, Siman 317, at the beginning, that this means specifically that it is intended to last forever (here, too, one can explain the logic simply: since that was the case in the Mishkan, where all matters of sewing and connection were intended to remain that way forever). In the case at hand, we must add that with a needle, and especially a safety pin, one

## 259

can see tangibly in all the matters for which they are used for connection that it is impossible for them to remain that way forever.
c) The use of a safety pin is, in most cases, specifically for the needs of the day, in which case we are lenient with two Rabbinic prohibitions even *lechatchilah*, as is brought in many places. Based on all the above, in my opinion, there is no room for objection at all to a single fastening of a safety pin, and there is room to say that even two or three fastenings are permitted, and at the very least, it is no more than a Rabbinic matter.

I have not elaborated on all the above as required, for they have already elaborated on this in the discussion in *Gevuros Ram*, Siman 17-19, in the book *Tal Oros*, which holds the opinion of the respondent, and in the book *Orchos Chaim* (the new one), Siman 340, and the collection of all opinions on this in the book *Ketzos HaShulchan* by Rabbi Avraham Chaim Naeh, Part 8, Siman 146, Se'if 12—see there at length regarding all the above.
Incidentally, regarding what your honor noted as proof from the aforementioned *Menachos*, this aligns with the opinion of the *Gedolim* in the *Kuntres Acharon* of the *Shulchan Aruch* of our Rebbe, Siman 301, at the end, as was also noted in *Ketzos HaShulchan*...
(From a letter dated 21 Elul, 5715)

In response to your letter, which is a continuation of the discussion regarding metal wire and sewing with it concerning the *halachos* of Shabbos. Your honor brings several sources from our Sages in your letter that use the term *tefirah* or *chayta* (sewing in Aramaic), even though it is a metal wire and the like.
It is puzzling, for is "sewing" written in the Torah regarding the prohibitions of Shabbos? We learn the liabilities of Shabbos from the *melachah* of the Mishkan, and it does not matter if they are called "sewing" or not, but rather whether the *melachah* was in the Mishkan or at least performed in its usual manner. Even though the Mishnah uses the term "sews" (*tofer*), it is because "the greater includes the lesser" (*bichlal ma'atayim maneh*), but the lesser does not include the greater. Just as with the other terms of the Mishnah, it is specifically in the manner that it was in the Mishkan and in its usual way, and this is simple.

Incidentally, although it is irrelevant to the above, regarding what you noted from the verse "and they sewed fig leaves," even though they did not have silk or wool threads or the like, and therefore you learn that it refers to a manner of sewing that is not the usual way in our days—and the material does not matter—if so, one could also say that surely they did not have a needle, and consequently they sewed with their fingers, meaning they made a hole with a fingernail, etc., and on this basis, one would be liable for sewing that is exempt according to all opinions. Regarding the facts, it is *tzarich iyun* (requires study) where you got the idea that they did not have silk or wool threads, etc. It is only simple that they did not have a metal wire, which is what we are discussing, for the grandson of Adam was a "forger of every cutting instrument of copper and iron."

Similarly, regarding what you wrote that there is no difference between *kilayim* and Shabbos regarding the material with which one fastens the stitches:

## 260

In my opinion, the opposite is simple, for in *kilayim*, it does not matter in what manner the connection is made, only the reality that it was made—the connection. In Shabbos, it is the opposite: the entire prohibition depends only on whether the manner in which the *melachah* is performed is its usual way, etc.
Regarding what you noted about my phrasing "to cause so many of the kosher daughters of Israel, etc."—where do I get that this is the custom of the daughters of Israel? I anchored my position in the *Korban Nesanel* and the books that followed it, that this is how they practiced in the communities of Israel, etc., for the law is the same for a safety pin as it is in our generation or in the manners brought in the *Korban Nesanel* and the books that followed it...
Regarding what your honor wrote from *Shabbos* (74b) and elsewhere: according to your reasoning, if you compare a safety pin to that, then you must simply say he is liable for a *chatas*, etc. You must also admit that it is not comparable, and the reason is that there is no sewing with a needle, and in the Mishkan, there were threads.
From *Shabbos* (48b) it is proven that one should not learn Shabbos from *kilayim*, because sewing that is not permanent is not sewing or connection on Shabbos (and see there in the *Hagahos Maimoniyos*). The reason is as above.
Regarding what you asked in *Tosafos* (s.v. *d'yada*, *Shabbos* 69a), how is it possible that he knew about the positive commandment of Shabbos and did not know about the negative commandment, since the fulfillment of the positive commandment is by means of keeping the negative commandment—I did not understand the question, for the meaning there is that he did not know that there is a negative commandment in the Torah regarding this. Regarding the assumption itself that the fulfillment of the positive commandment of "you shall rest" is only by means of keeping the negative commandment—see Rambam, *Hilchos Shabbos*, beginning of Chapter 21.
(From a letter dated 10 Nissan, 5716)

...Regarding what you write concerning the electric lamp, among many who are G-d-fearing, the custom in such cases is to fix a "Shabbos clock." Although there are those who are extremely stringent and doubt even this permissibility, for which reason I refrain from giving advice officially, you, for your part, should endeavor in this, without making a *tummel* (commotion). Therefore, it is worthwhile that you investigate where you can obtain such a clock, which is certainly found in abundance in Tel Aviv, and especially among the G-d-fearing Ashkenazic circles, who have been accustomed to this for generations. You should purchase the clock at my expense, and it is understood that I must cover all the expenses, meaning the price of the clock and also its installation in the necessary place in the house where it is located, after you inform me. After you do this, I am confident that you will succeed in having them agree to the matter, and consequently, it will also be easier to implement this in the other institutions of the *Melben*, and a word to the wise is sufficient...
(From a letter dated 3 Teves, 5716)

In response to your letter, in which you ask if you should purchase a business in partnership with another who does not keep Shabbos, in a manner where the business will also not be kept on Shabbos, except that it will be on the share of the other person.

## 261

Surely you know that money connected with the desecration of Shabbos, Heaven forbid, not only goes to waste, but also drags other money along with it. If so, what do you have to do with such businesses that are very, very close to loss and far from profit?!
May the Almighty, who feeds and sustains everyone, surely provide you with your livelihood in abundance in a kosher manner, and in a way that you will be able to use your livelihood for *gezunte zachen un yiddishe zachen* (healthy things and Jewish things).
(From a letter dated 9 Iyar, 5711)

I have received your letter from *Motzaei Shabbos Kodesh* *Parshas Mikeitz*, in which you write about the incident caused by the mistake of the paper regarding the time of candle lighting:
You should distribute to *tzedakah*, over the course of a few weeks, $7.02 (seven dollars and two cents), and it is better to do this on *Erev Shabbos* before candle lighting. Also, study the laws of Shabbos in the *Kitzur Shulchan Aruch*—as far as I know, there is a *Kitzur Shulchan* translated into English as well, so it will likely be easier for you to learn from the English translation. It would be very appropriate if you were to invite a few more women to learn together. You should also let go of the thought (distract your mind) of the whole matter, and you should check the *mezuzos* of your house once again.
(From a letter dated 8 Teves, 5712)


## הוספה

## 261

### Supplement

[The following was provided by the Rebbe as a supplement to Likkutei Sichos, Parshas Yisro (18 Shevat), 5748].

A manuscript booklet has come into our possession containing discourses and maamarim of the Mitteler Rebbe. For the benefit of the many, we are transcribing the following entry (page 86b) :

The reason we place the chassan under the chuppah on the day of his wedding is because the chuppah represents the level of makif. Everything he will engage in regarding avodas Hashem throughout his life is drawn to him from the makif at that moment. Therefore, he must connect his thoughts to Hashem at that time, for through this he will draw from the makif then, etc., and a word to the wise is sufficient. 5778.


## משפטים

## 262

### Mishpatim

Regarding the point raised in Bava Kamma, in the Mishnah at the beginning of the eighth chapter—to resolve the commentary of Rashi regarding the *eved ivri* (Hebrew slave) who is appraised—based on the notes of the Ma’adanei Yom Tov and Tosafos R’ Akiva Eiger—this is also stated in Tiferes Yaakov on the Mishnayos there.

And to note regarding his comment: 
a) Surely one who sells himself also goes free in the Yovel. 
b) The explanation of the Mishnah must be consistent for the Rabbis just as it is for Rabbi Eliezer, who holds that even one who sells himself is only for six years (Kiddushin 14b). 

And what appears to me regarding Rashi’s commentary—that he rejects the interpretation that he is appraised like a *eved kenaani* (Canaanite slave)—is that the Jewish people do not have such a valuation, since it is forbidden to work him with the labor of a slave, as we are commanded regarding him, "he is well with you," and so on. Therefore, the explanation must be specifically "like a *eved kenaani*," and as per the note (question) of the Ma’adanei Yom Tov—one must calculate the difference between selling in installments and selling all at once, and deduct accordingly. And this is clear.

(From a letter dated 28 Shevat, 5720)


## עניני רפואה

## 262

### Medical Matters

In response to your letter from the 14th of Cheshvan (and the one preceding it), in which you ask:

1) Whether it is permitted to engage in medical treatment only for a sick person, or if it is also permitted to use those medicines that prevent illness—that is to say, those that fortify health so that one does not become ill.

It is a daily occurrence that even the great figures of Israel and its leaders do this. See also *Hilchos Deios* by the Rambam, Chapter 4. Furthermore, the verse explicitly states: "All the sickness... I will not place upon you, for I am Hashem your healer," which implies that this, too, is included in the category of healing.

2) Regarding those substances that are injected into the body, whether it is permitted to use them—it seems your question concerns those made from non-kosher materials.

Here, too, it is a daily occurrence that G-d-fearing and pious people act in this manner without any hesitation. After all, it is permitted to benefit from things that are forbidden to eat but permitted for benefit.

3) How to conduct oneself regarding the Salk vaccine, which they are now beginning to inject into children.

They have already been doing this here for several months, and as mentioned above, this is also the case in the most pious circles. That is to say, there is no question here regarding kashrus or the like, but it is understood that one must verify that the vaccine is from a good, reliable laboratory.

It is understood that a separate matter is blood transfusion, which has become common recently and is becoming more and more prevalent, where there is no scrutiny at all as to who the donor is. Logically, this is more "mentally dulling" (*metamtem*) than what is written in *Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah*, end of Chapter 81, in the *Hagah*. Perhaps the reason for the lack of scrutiny in this matter is:

## 263

Because transfusions are frequently used for patients who are in danger, or at the very least, seriously ill. Furthermore, it is a one-time event—unlike the case in *Yoreh Deah* mentioned there.

— To note: The bloodletting mentioned in the *Gemara*—in most cases, it refers to a healthy person who is letting blood.

For the laws of medicine, see *Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah*, Chapters 155, 336...
(From a letter dated 24th of Mar-Cheshvan, 5717)

---

I was distressed to hear of the panic and the rushing to doctors throughout the entire day for something that has no basis. It is also surprising that her husband, the Rabbi, may he live, is involved in this—why and for what reason are they using such haste where it is not needed? While generally, diligence is a virtue, apart from the fact that panic is in any case a deficiency, diligence is also not appropriate in every situation. They should be confident in the Ribono shel Olam, who creates, sustains, and gives life to the entire world and all that is in it, and especially to every single man and woman of Israel, His close ones, that He will send her the proper health. Together with her husband, the Rabbi, may he live, they will raise their son, may he live, to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds. Although one needs a vessel in the way of nature for everything—that is, to ask a doctor’s opinion and follow his instructions—the *farkahkeit* (worrying) about it, the pilpul, the back-and-forth regarding the doctors' opinions, and the deep immersion in medical science and its matters, this is not a matter for them, but only for those whose livelihood depends on it, so that they can perform their work faithfully according to the Torah's command, "He shall surely heal." But as for the rest, they should use their intellect and the power of understanding and knowledge with which the Ribono shel Olam has graced them, whether in matters of Torah and mitzvos or in optional matters that can be transformed into a matter of mitzvah. But worry and melancholy (*marah shechorah*) are things that harm health—both physical health and spiritual health—and they distract and confuse them from fulfilling their role and mission in this world. May the Ribono shel Olam grant her and her husband, the Rabbi, may he live, to have the characteristics of "a hasty people" (*am paziza*) in matters of Torah and mitzvos, and patience and composure in their other affairs. May it be for success in both material and spiritual matters.

With a blessing for proper health.
(From a letter dated 12th of Sivan, 5712)

---

I received your letter in due time regarding the health condition of your son... may he live, who is worried about the opinion of one doctor who discouraged him and weakened his hope for a complete recovery for his son, may he live:

Surely you are aware of the statement of several of our Nasi'im, our holy Rebbes, regarding the Sages' teaching, "He shall surely heal,"

## 264

that permission was given to the doctor to heal. This is the only power and authority the doctor has—to heal in matters of medicine. Especially since the second doctor does not agree with the pessimistic opinion, you should therefore not weaken your good hope at all. This is especially true in these days, when new medicines and new methods in medical matters are being discovered every single day.

At a time of grace, when I am at the resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, I will mention your son, may he live, for healing. My hope is strong that in time you will be able to bring me good news regarding this. But it goes without saying that, G-d forbid, you must not weaken your trust in the Ribono shel Olam, who is the Healer of the sick, and there is no obstacle for Him to save, whether with much or with little. Through an increase in strength in trust, both from your side and from the side of your wife, may she live, there is no doubt that this will also hasten the improvement of your son's health, may he live.

It is appropriate that you take upon yourself additional study in Torah in general, and in the teachings of Chassidus in particular, as well as giving to tzedakah—even if only small amounts, but regularly and frequently—for the merit of your son, may he live. I will await good news from you regarding the above...
(From a letter dated 22nd of Iyar, 5711)

May the Almighty help that the operation goes well, and that you will be able to report good news regarding it.

It would be a good thing if you could keep a kosher mezuzah with you in your room at the hospital, and also take upon yourself that as soon as you leave the hospital, you will give something to tzedakah for *Rabbeinu Meir Baal HaNes* every Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov, and say a chapter of Tehillim every day in Lashon HaKodesh, or if that is difficult for you, then in English.

I hope to hear good news that things are going better for you, and I conclude with a blessing.
(From a letter dated Rosh Chodesh Shevat, 5712)

---

In response to your letter, in which you inform me that you have been studying at the yeshiva in Sefaria for two years and two months, and a doctor is advising you to have your tonsils removed and is advising you to do it now, and you also request a blessing for your father, may he live...

Regarding the surgery: consult one more doctor who is an expert in this field. If he also agrees to perform the surgery, and now, then may it be His will that the surgery goes well and at a propitious and successful time. On the Shabbos before the surgery, you should say the entire Tehillim—if possible without interruption, meaning even without saying the *Yehi Ratzon* except after all the books—and when you know the day of the surgery for certain, inform me here.
(From a letter dated 1st of Shevat, 5712)

---

I have received your letter of the 24th of Teves, in which you describe your situation, and that you have seen the report from the doctor and how it has affected you, and how you are imagining the future, and therefore you are saying Tehillim and praying to the Ribono shel Olam, and you ask for my opinion:

Answer:
The fact that you are saying Tehillim and praying to the Ribono shel Olam is certainly good, for He, blessed be He, is the Master of the entire world and of every person with all their details. But the fact that you write that you have been thinking about the doctor's report and imagining the future, I do not agree with you, for that does not belong to you at all, and it is not for that purpose that you were created.

The Rabbi... writes to me that you are a Jew, a person of Torah and mitzvos. Consequently, it is certain that you believe that Hashem Yisbarach is the *Adon Olam*—the Master of the world. We see even in human management, when one is a good manager, that everything is organized so that one thing does not interfere with another, and every part of the management serves the purpose for which it was created. If this is true for a human being who is limited in all his affairs and can therefore sometimes make a mistake, then *kal v'chomer* it is certainly true for the Ribono shel Olam's management, that every thing, wherever it is found, must fulfill its goal and perfection—its completion—in its mission. When one grabs hold of doing another matter, there are two deficiencies in this: a) since it is not suited to its matter, it only causes damage, and b) it pulls away—turns away—from fulfilling the mission for which it is truly intended.

All of the above is also applicable to your situation. For many reasons, which are certainly by *Hashgacha Pratis*, your profession is not that of a physician. Having been raised as a Jew who observes Torah and mitzvos, we know two things: a) medical matters are not your mission from Hashem in this world, and b) observing Torah and mitzvos, which also includes the mitzvah of "Love your neighbor as yourself," "You shall surely rebuke," etc., and also as it says in the book *Tanna D'bei Eliyahu*, "When you see a naked person, you shall clothe him"—that when you see a Jew who is "naked" of Torah and mitzvos, you must strive to clothe him with Torah and mitzvos—that this is your goal and the mission for which you were created.

From this, it is understandable that when you speculate and offer opinions in medical science, firstly, it turns you away from fulfilling your mission for which you are destined. Secondly, in these matters of medicine, you can, G-d forbid, only cause damage, but in no way can you fix anything. The damage in this can be, G-d forbid, because from agitation, you imagine things that will not happen, and consequently, this weakens your *mazal* and weakens your trust in Hashem Yisbarach through your overthinking and delving into what the doctor said, and what that professor might think, etc.

As you ask for my opinion, I tell you that you must conduct yourself as the holy Torah demands. The Torah says that it—the Torah—has given permission to heal, meaning the Torah has given permission for people to turn to doctors, and has given permission and possibility to the doctors only to heal and fix the person. Therefore, the world conducts itself such that one goes to a doctor and then does what they instruct to do. You have nothing more to do in this, and you should leave it to the doctor. What you must do is be certain in Hashem Yisbarach that you will have long life and years. According to what is written in the verse, "The fear of Hashem leads to life," the stronger your trust in Hashem Yisbarach is, and the fewer doubts you have in this, and the more you devote yourself to fulfilling your mission in the world—as mentioned earlier—to observe Torah and mitzvos and also to influence others in this direction, the more long life and years you will have, literally, without any "twisting" of the meaning. Forget entirely about the report and what you have read in medical books, because that is not your mission and it does not belong to you at all. Since it does not belong to you, it cannot make you better, and in general, it only makes things worse, G-d forbid.

You should see to saying a *Yom Tehillim* (as the Tehillim is divided for the days of the month) every day after davening in the morning, and study Chumash with Rashi every day, and also take part in the *shiurim* that are studied in public, where at least one of the *shiurim* should be the study of Chassidus. And it goes without saying, to set yourself the goal as it says in the verse, and as the holy Baal Shem Tov demanded of Chassidim: "Serve Hashem with joy." "Serve" means in davening and learning, and also in eating and drinking, and all the other things a person does, and even with sleeping, as the Rambam writes in *Hilchos Deios*. When you do this, you will begin to feel better and better, and you will become healthier and healthier, and you will be able to report good news to me regarding this.

It would also be good if every day before davening in the morning and before Mincha, you would give a few pennies to tzedakah (obviously, except for Shabbos and Yom Tov).

I hope and am certain that you will accept my suggestion and instructions as stated, and will let me know about all this as soon as possible.

With a blessing for good health and a speedy recovery, and may you be able to fulfill your mission in this world with peace of mind and peace of body for long, good years, and to be a Chassid...
(From a letter dated 27th of Teves, 5712)

---

In response to your letter of the 17th of Sivan, I was alarmed to read the beginning, that it is very difficult for you, etc., and "Why do you involve yourself in the hidden matters of the Merciful One?" Regarding what you quote from the Rambam that the Holy One, blessed be He, does not perform a miracle that departs from the way of nature for an individual person—we have seen with our own eyes miracles that depart from the way of nature even for individual people, especially in recent years. This is especially true in matters concerning the human body, where many times they have erred even after all the tests. This is in addition to the fact that new medicines are being discovered from day to day. However, it is necessary and impossible otherwise to strengthen the connection with Hashem Yisbarach, the Healer of all flesh, who does wonders. The "Scripture" does not depart from its literal meaning, that He does wonders for an individual person, and the proof for this is that everyone individually recites this blessing. Elaborating on this is superfluous. If only they would not fulfill the matter of "He who increases knowledge," etc., in such matters; it is better to fulfill the Sages' teaching that "the beneficiary of a miracle does not recognize his miracle." It is understood that all the above does not at all negate the logic that one must know the opinion of at least two doctors in this field and their opinion regarding procedures, as is known from the statement of the Tzemach Tzedek that the Torah says there is permission for a doctor to heal, but not, G-d forbid, to cause melancholy, etc.
(From a letter dated 21st of Sivan, 5713)

---

## 268

In response to your letter of the 2nd of Shvat, in which you inform me of the health condition of your wife, may she live: when I am at the resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, I will mention her, and surely he will awaken great mercy for her.

Surely she has received some instructions from the doctor and is following them. I would be interested to know if, besides what you write regarding *bitter salt* and magnesia, you also know about radiation or surgery. For even though He is the Healer of all flesh and does wonders, nevertheless, it is customary that there should also be some hold in nature, even if it is very slight. As I once heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that a very sick person once came to the Alter Rebbe, and he healed him with a piece of *matzah shemurah* and half a glass of water. Thus, at the very least, there must be some hold in nature. May the Ribono shel Olam hear your prayer and request, and may you be able to inform me of good news.
(From a letter dated 27th of Sivan, 5711)

---

...Regarding what you wrote concerning a toothache, and the doctors are advising to extract it, etc.—although it is known from the Sages (*Pesachim* 113a) regarding the extraction of teeth (and there are Chassidim who tell that this is why the great Rabbi, the great Chassid, and the great Tzaddik, R. Hillel of Paritch, of blessed memory, was careful not to extract a tooth), I have not seen people being careful about this, not even in the house of the Rebbe. It is understood according to what is known regarding the medicines in the *Gemara*, and that the natures have changed. Moreover, it is forbidden to experiment with this, as is brought from the Maharil (*Rema* to *Yoreh Deah*, Chapter 336).

By the way, I once heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that this is the only incantation for someone who has a bone stuck, etc. (*Shabbos* 67a), which they used to teach even to the children in the Rebbe's house. In times of need, G-d forbid, they would say it with the preface of placing a bowl on the head. Therefore, although it is a matter of question whether one should do this as a last resort, what one doctor advises—to extract all the teeth, G-d forbid—should not be done, but rather consult with other experts in this, and perhaps one or two is enough, etc.
(From a letter dated 19th of Iyar, 5716)

---

I received your regards through... that, thank G-d, your health and eyesight have improved. Surely you will continue to guard the matters I wrote to you about in the future. It would be very good if you would add to your daily study, or have someone study before you, a few lines in the holy *Zohar* and a few lines in the holy *Tanya*, in which the expression "Come and see" (*Ta Chazi*) is common. This is the command of our holy Torah, that one should see Elokus

## 269

tangibly, which is also a remedy and medicine for the physical eyesight as it should be, and to see how they were created and are sustained by the word of Hashem, the power of the Actor in the acted-upon.
(From a letter dated 18th of Sivan, 5713)

---

In response to your letter in which you write about your health condition, and especially regarding your eye: surely you will continue to follow the doctors' instructions in this, and the Ribono shel Olam will send His word and heal you.

It is surely superfluous to remind you of the Sages' teaching that being careful with Kiddush and Havdalah adds especially regarding a person's eyesight, as well as increasing the study of the teachings of Chassidus on Shabbos. By way of a play on words, one could say that this is the hint in the Sages' teaching that "a large stride takes away..."—that the burning of the "coarseness" (*gasus*) and its transformation comes through immersion in the waters of the teachings of Chassidus, *tevilah* (immersion) being synonymous with *bitul* (nullification).
(From a letter dated 26th of Adar II, 5714)

---

...I received news regarding your health condition, and my hope is strong that everything was in order and successful, and you will bring me good news in this. It is surely superfluous to remind you of the Sages' teaching that anyone who is careful with the wine of Kiddush and the wine of Havdalah adds to his eyesight.

In the days of the month of Elul, the accounting of the entire year, one should also say this by way of hint and moral lesson: that anyone who is careful with the wine (the wine enters, the intellect and understanding—the secret of man and creation goes out and is revealed) of Kiddush (in that which he must sanctify in his life and in his portion of the world through "do good" (positive mitzvos)) and in Havdalah (in that which he must separate and distinguish himself from this through "turn from evil" (negative mitzvos)), this adds to a person's eyesight, so that he will see the truth in all his surroundings and within himself, the truth of Hashem forever. As the Rambam says (beginning of *Yesodei HaTorah*), He alone is the Truth and there is no other truth like His truth (and before that), and all existing things were only found from the truth of His existence.

With a blessing for a speedy recovery, good news, and a good inscription and sealing.

And in Havdalah, it is through the songs, since "until the time of the end that I will remove the spirit of impurity from

## 270

the earth"—it is only that they delay the calamities, as the language of *Pirkei DeRabbi Eliezer*, and not that they are completely abolished from the entire earth, which is the action of the mitzvah itself. And this is not the place to elaborate.
(From a letter dated 10th of Elul, 5715)

---

...Your notification regarding Mrs. ..., may she live, that they decided to perform surgery on her one eye without waiting a long time: may it be His will from the Ribono shel Olam that the surgery goes well and she returns to her strength soon. I do not know the custom there, but if there is a *ner tamid* in the synagogue, she should participate in this (but not to fix it from the start). If there is no such arrangement there, she should take upon herself for some time the provision of the candles in the synagogue. Surely she lights candles on Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov, and it is good that she set aside for the tzedakah of *Rambeah"n* (Rabbi Meir Baal HaNes) before lighting the candles.
(From a letter dated 23rd of Teves, 5712)

---

...Regarding your son..., may he live, who has a tendency toward theft, G-d forbid, you must turn to a doctor in this field, for this is a form of weakness, and there are now medical means for this. It is understood not to neglect saying a chapter of Tehillim every day (in addition to the regular order), and also to give a *prutah* or three to tzedakah before the morning and Mincha prayers for the merit of your son specifically. Also, check the *tzitzis* on the tallis katan of your son, may he live, and that he should not go with his head uncovered. Check the *mezuzos* in your home. If it is customary among the students that they go with a covering under the hat, you should accustom him to this without it being conspicuous, and that it should come from the suggestion of his friends. I hope that you will be able to report good news in this.
(From a letter dated 27th of Teves, 5712)


## המשך פ' משפטים

## 270

Regarding the difficulty raised against the *Prishah* in *Choshen Mishpat* 359:3, who explains that the *shinui* (change in behavior) of a lion is that it tears its prey, but the subsequent eating is its natural way—whereas for him (the questioner), the opposite seems more logical:

While the language of Rashi (*Bava Kamma* 16b, s.v. *v’hachtiv*) might slightly imply that the *shinui* lies in the eating, it is impossible to say so, because the *Gemara* there resolves the matter by saying that the lion reconsidered and ate it. If the *shinui* were in the eating, what would be gained by the fact that it reconsidered?

## 271

Furthermore, the logic supports the *Prishah*. A lion tears its prey for its cubs and its lair, and eats it afterward—this is its natural behavior (*neveilos*). It is only when it is hungry that it does not wait until the animal dies, because it is the "king of beasts," etc., as stated in the *Prishah*. If we see that it waits, that is the opposite of its natural way.

The *Sha’ar HaGilyon* also writes in accordance with the *Prishah*.

(From a letter dated 12 Adar, 5715)

In response to your letter, in which you write about your spiritual state and your desire to rectify your deficiencies in matters of *yiras shamayim*, the *avodah* of *tefillah*, and the study of Torah:

It is a well-known teaching of our Sages regarding the aforementioned: "If one says, 'I have labored and not found,' do not believe him; 'I have not labored and found,' do not believe him; 'I have labored and found,' believe him." From this, it is understood that the matter depends on the person himself, provided that he labors in it, and according to his own capacity.

It is unnecessary to remind you—as this has already been publicized in several letters and subsequently in *maamarim* of *Chassidus*—that this is not the path: through fasts and self-afflictions (*sigufim*) in a manner that weakens one’s health. Rather, it is "you shall surely help with him" (*azov ta’azov imo*)—together with the body and the *nefesh habehamis*. The *sigufim* must be of the *nefesh habehamis*, not of the human body, which is the property of the *Ribono shel Olam*, as is explained in many places. See *Hilchos Nizkei HaGuf* by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe—who rules in the *nistar* (hidden) aspects of Torah—and the *Shulchan Aruch*—which rules in the *nigleh* (revealed) aspects of Torah. The *sigufim* of the *nefesh habehamis* consist of: restraining one’s mouth from speaking idle words, and even delaying necessary words for a certain time or for a few moments, as well as guarding the sense of sight, etc., as explained in many places (including *Sefer HaToldos* of the Rebbe Maharash, page 72, at the end). You should consult with a *mashpia* of *Chassidus* in your vicinity; it would be best to consult with the *Harav HaChassid*... a *mashpia* of *Chassidus* at Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod. It is unnecessary to explain that all of the above is by way of addition to your regular *shiurim* in the study of *Chassidus* and the *nigleh* aspects of Torah. May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant you success.

(From a letter dated 11 Adar, 5714)

I have received your request for a blessing of *refuah* (healing) for one of your students... and your second piece of news, that the surgery took place and everything is in order. May it be the will of the *Ribono shel Olam* that just as you bring good news regarding the results in the physical realm, so too may you bring good news regarding the results in the spiritual realm—that your students are healthy as they should be in their spiritual lives.

Since for a Jewish person, the physical and the spiritual go hand in hand, one might say, by way of a *melitzah* (homiletical interpretation), based on what our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe writes in *Iggeres HaTeshuvah*, Chapter 3, that in these generations we are not as healthy as

## 272

those in the earlier generations, and consequently, excessive fasting is harmful, as it may lead to illness or physical pain, *chas v’shalom*—so too is it regarding the healing of the soul. If in earlier generations it was possible to suffice with the order of *sigufim* in the spiritual sense—that is, matters of *mussar* that humble a person and cause him distress, etc.—in our generations, this could lead to illness or pain, or even "spiritual pain," meaning that he may fall further in his spirit, or become despondent, *chas v’shalom*, or that the body, the *nefesh habehamis*, and the *yetzer hara* will rebel against this humiliation. Therefore, it is necessary to hold fast to the path taught by the Baal Shem Tov, "you shall surely help with him" (*azov ta’azov imo*). This begins with the explanation that the *neshamah* is truly a "part of Elokus from above," for He and His wisdom are one, and consequently, the emissary of the Supreme One is like Him (see *Likutei Torah*, beginning of *Parshas Vayikra* on this). A person is given the highest powers, not only to overcome obstacles but also to illuminate his soul, his body, and his portion in the world with additional light, and to make them vessels for *Elokus* out of joy. Consequently, it is a pity to waste his time and the powers he is not utilizing, the cause of which is the degradation of his body, etc. Joy breaks through barriers—even the barriers of his body and his *nefesh habehamis*.

How wondrous is the precision in the ruling of the *Rema* in *Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chayim*, 98:1 (end): "And he should think before the *tefillah* about the greatness of the *E-l Yisbarach* (and only afterward) about the lowliness of man." It is known that even the order of things in the Torah is itself Torah. If it is incumbent upon him to instill this order in his students, how much more so must these matters be "moist enough to moisten others" (*tofeach al menas lehatfiach*) within himself. There is nothing that can stand before the will, even when one needs to change habits that have already become second nature.

(From a letter dated 19 Adar, 5714)


## תרומה

## 273

### Terumah

In response to your letter, regarding your question: In Torah Or, Parshas Terumah (p. 70a), in the *maamar* beginning "Aval," there is a parenthetical note concerning the time of *galus*, stating that the aspect of the *ha'arah* (illumination) departed "to its *shoresh* (root) and its *makor* (source) in *Atzilus*." You ask: what is its *shoresh* and what is its *makor*?

This *maamar* corresponds to the statement in the *Zohar* that in *galus*, *Kudsha Brich Hu* ascends higher and higher. This has been explained in many places: *Kudsha Brich Hu* refers to *Ze'er Anpin* (the *z'eir anpin zutri* mentioned in the *Torah Or* there); "higher" refers to *Binah*; and "higher still" refers to *Atik*, which is *Keter*. This is understood based on what is explained in *Tikkunei Zohar*, *Tikkun* 49, that *Binah* is called the *shoresh* of the tree. Furthermore, in *Ra'aya Meheimna*, *Parshas Bo* (42b), it is stated that *Keter* is called the *makor* (see the explanation in *Likutei Torah*, *Vayikra* 52a). It can also be explained simply through the distinction between the terms *shoresh* and *makor*, as is understood in places where both are cited, to indicate a difference in levels: the *shoresh* is found in closer proximity and is of the essence of the matters that stem from the *shoresh*, whereas the *makor* is at a distance from that which comes from the *makor*.

Based on the above, the discussion in the *nigleh* (revealed Torah) in the *sefer Gidulei Taharah*, in the *Responsa* at the end of the book (Section 2), regarding the explanation of the terms *bor* (pit), *ma'ayan* (spring), and *makor* (source)—concluding that *makor* refers to the inherent power, etc.—is also clarified. This corresponds to the order of the *Sefiros*: *Keter*, *Chochma*, and *Binah* are the *makor*, *ma'ayan*, and *bor* (or *shoresh*)...

(From a letter dated 21 Adar, 5716)


## תצוה

## 274

### Tetzaveh

... *Divrei Yatziv* at the end. The opinion of the Rambam regarding the priestly garments when not engaged in the *avodah*. His words require study, for the Rambam explicitly writes that it is permitted to derive benefit from the priestly garments even before the *avodah*, with the exception of the *avnet*, which is forbidden because of *shaatnez* (*Hilchos Klei HaMikdash* 8:11-12. And see *Tosafos Yeshanim* to *Yoma* 69a, s.v. *v'tifuk*). However, his words are relevant to the opinion of the *Tosafos* in *Yoma* there.
(From a letter dated 2 Kislev, 5717)

... Regarding what was written concerning the *Shaar Rosh Hashanah v'Yom HaKippurim* by the Mitteler Rebbe, that the *michnasayim* of the *Kohen Gadol* reached down to his heels.
This was pointed out to me some time ago, and upon searching through the manuscripts, the aforementioned *maamar* has not yet been found. However, I did find a *maamar* from the Tzemach Tzedek on those same topics, which also explains the matter of the garments, and there, the words discussing the length of the *michnasayim* are not present.
(From a letter dated 27 Tammuz, 5718)


## אדר

## 275

### Adar

... Regarding the question based on the statement of our Sages, "When Adar enters, we increase in joy," etc., and the fact that his *mazal* is strong—how, then, did it happen that in this very month, Moshe Rabbeinu, the shepherd of Israel, passed away?

The answer is understood from the discussion in the Gemara (Megillah 13b), where there was a line of reasoning to decide the month of Adar for both sides. As our Sages state there, since the *pur* (lot) fell in the month of Adar, etc., but the conclusion was that he did not know, etc.—this decided and determined the entire month, for which it is said, "And it was turned about."

2) Regarding the question concerning the apparent contradiction with the statement of our Sages regarding the passing of *tzaddikim*, that it is as difficult as the day, etc., and why we call this day a *hillula*, etc.

The *acharonim* have already written extensively on this, and many explanations have been offered; see there (collected in *Sdei Chemed*, *Asifat Dinim*, *Ma'arechet Eretz Yisrael*, subsection 6, and *Pe'at HaSadeh* there; in the book *Hillula d'Rashbi* by Rabbi Margolies. See also *Likutei HaShas* of the Arizal to *Berachos* 6b; Rashi to *Yevamos* 122a; *Rosh* to *Yevamos* 113a—that it is a term for *Yom Tov*. And others).

(From a letter, 16 Shevat, 5720)

... We are currently in the days that connect one redemption to another, and the wondrous Rashi is well known (and I have known his vitality in the language of Rashi), *Ta'anis* 29a, end of side a, s.v. *Mishenichnas Adar*: "These were days of miracles for Israel, Purim and Pesach." This proves that they are one and the same; on the contrary, they are named after Adar, in which was born and shone the radiance of the first and final Redeemer—for the redemption of Egypt and "as in the days of your coming out, etc., I will show him wonders"—in the future redemption. Since, through having fulfilled what they had already accepted in the days of Purim in Adar—whereby the "great protest" against the Torah was naturally nullified—the inner soul of the Jewish person, which was always faithful to him, is unified. As is known from the Maharal, based on what the Rambam writes in *Hilchos Geirushin*, end of chapter 2, with the outer aspect of the soul—which is the vessel for the revelation of the unity of the hidden aspect of Torah with the revealed, and for the unity and revelation of the hidden aspect of the *Kudsha Brich Hu* with the revealed aspect of the *Kudsha Brich Hu*—which is the concept of the complete and true redemption, "for all will know Me, from the smallest to the greatest" (*Shaar HaEmunah*, ch. 15 and onwards).

(From a letter, 5 Nissan, 5715)

... It is known from our Sages, "When Adar enters, we increase in joy" (brought as *halacha* in *Magen Avraham*, *Orach Chaim* 586:6. See also *Responsa Chasam Sofer*, *Orach Chaim*, subsection 60, and *Nimukei Orach Chaim* there—by the author of *Minchat Ani*). And according to what is written in the *Rema*, *Orach Chaim* 568:7, it is from the beginning of Adar. And thus, according to the *Responsa* of the Geonim and the *Maharitz Gi'at* (brought in *Tur Orach Chaim* 520; and see in the book [that] are brought in *Sdei Chemed*, *Pe'at HaSadeh*, *Kelalim*, subsection 82), there is a *chazakah* (presumption) of joy three times: Adar, Rosh Chodesh, and the joy of *Chag HaShavuos*. And a *chazakah* applies to the future as well.

(From a letter, 23 Shevat, 5714)

... May it be the will that, as we find ourselves in the month of Adar, regarding every day of which it is said that we increase in joy—from which it is understood that the matters of Adar that bring about joy, i.e., the matters of the *Megillah*, have influenced all the days of the month—that at the very least now, the matter will be revealed that "the common people become Jews." And if so, *kal v'chomer* regarding those hinted at by the second *yud*, as discussed at the Purim *farbrengen* in the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov and the Tzemach Tzedek that we heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zya".*

Parenthetically, it should be noted that the matter of the explanation of the two *yudin* is also hinted at in the revealed part of Torah. It is my long-held position that everything discussed in the revealed part has its counterpart in the hidden, and what is said in the hidden has its counterpart in the revealed, in the teaching of our Sages on the verse "And He fashioned" with two *yudin*. See also the *Hagahos* of the Tzemach Tzedek, page 81 and onwards.

(From a letter, 19 Adar, 5720)

... And may the *Ribono shel Olam* grant us the merit, beginning from this day, Rosh Chodesh, to see that "And it was turned about"—that the Jews (the power of faith—see *Megillah*, beginning of page 13) will have dominion (dominion and rule, in the body and in the world, and not merely as an encompassing light—see *Tanya*, beginning of chapter 13) over those who hate them (through the *is'hapcha* of their enemies from darkness to light—see *Likutei Torah*, *s.d. Hashem Li B'Ozrai*).

(From a letter, Rosh Chodesh Adar Sheni, 5711)

... We are in the month of Adar, which is the month of *segulah* (special virtue) in which it is said, "And it was turned about," etc., and "many of the common people become Jews," etc. And similarly in a subtle way, the matters of the "common people" (see *Likutei Torah*, *Devarim* 90d) are brought about in a way that they "become Jews" (and as our Sages say, anyone who denies idolatry is called a Jew). May it be the will that all this be accomplished with true expansion, both materially and spiritually.

(From a letter, 20 Adar, 5718)


## פורים — פסח

## 281

### Purim — Pesach

...I am interested to know if you are taking part in the Charedi life of your city, particularly regarding education. This is also a matter relevant to the days between Purim and Pesach, for the decree of Purim was nullified because Mordechai—the greatest of his generation in Torah, in yiras shamayim, and in wisdom—personally taught the children, as related by our Sages. This point is also central to the festival of Pesach, which begins with the Seder. We employ various methods to engage the hearts of the children, specifically to ensure they do not fall asleep (physically, and certainly not spiritually), and the Seder begins with the questions of the children. Similarly, the conclusion of the days of Pesach centers on the Splitting of the Sea, regarding which it is also related in Shemos Rabbah that they—the children who were born and raised in Mitzrayim—were the first to recognize Him (Hashem). The lesson to be drawn from this is that the redemption of Yisrael, both physically and spiritually, depends on the education of the younger generation. Every single Yid, even one as great as Mordechai—of whom our Sages said in Midrash Esther Rabbah that "Mordechai in his generation is like Moshe in his generation"—is personally obligated to take part in this education.

May the Ribono shel Olam enable each and every one of us to illuminate our portion of the world, through which we hasten and bring about the true and complete Geulah for all of Klal Yisrael, as explained in Tanya, Chapter 37. . .

(From a letter dated 28 Adar, 5712)


## תשא

## 282

### Tisa

In response to your letter in which you commented on the wonderful precision of Rashi’s language (Tisa 33:12), where he writes: "See, set your eyes and your heart upon your words." I, too, shall offer my portion regarding Rashi’s intent, and also the source from which Rashi derives this.

The ultimate purpose of Moshe’s aforementioned request was that even though Yisroel had sinned, the *Hashraas HaShechinah* should nevertheless remain among them—His very Essence and Being, not through an intermediary, and not even through another (see *Likutei Torah*, Tzav 12, 73c). This is as he concludes in the verse, "If Your Presence does not go... and we will be distinguished, I and Your people..." which is the concept of a *dirah lo yisbarach batachtonim* (a dwelling place for Him in the lower worlds), "And they shall make Me a sanctuary, and I will dwell within them"—within each and every one through the sanctuary. Consequently, we know Moshe’s intent from Hashem’s promise regarding the Beis HaMikdash, as it is said, "And My eyes and My heart shall be there all the days"—meaning, even at a time of *ritcha* (divine wrath).

With this, we can understand the puzzling *Yerushalmi* (Berachos, Chapter 4, Halacha 5): "His face is above, and His eyes and heart are below," see there. Based on this, we can also understand the precision of Rashi’s language, as well as his conclusion, "upon your words," which refers to the *sefirah* of *Malchus*. Through *Malchus* the world was created, and its purpose and inwardness is the Beis HaMikdash; for the totality of the world is a dwelling place for Him, and within the world itself, this is the concept of the Beis HaMikdash. Based on this, one can also explain the matter of "His eyes and His heart"—according to what is explained in *Tikkunei Zohar*, *Tikkun* 21, page 50b, and the *Razah D’Milah*, etc.

(From a letter dated 11 Nissan, 5713)

... Regarding what you transcribed in your letter concerning "Havayah Havayah," etc.: You did not explain the matters sufficiently. a) Regarding the words of the *Rosh*: since the thought of *avodah zarah* is joined [to the act], it is not "before he sinned." b) Regarding the interpretation of "Hashem Echad" which explains that they will not need anything but one Name: how is it possible to say that in the future there will not be the thirteen *tikkunei dikna* (rectifications of the beard), which are the thirteen *midos harachamim* (attributes of mercy), which, according to many of the *Rishonim*,

## 283

begin from the first Name of *Havayah*? On the contrary, it is precisely accurate from the language of our Sages, "I am He before he sins." The explanation of this is, in brief: a) According to what is written in *Tanya*, Chapter 16, regarding the precision of the term "joins" (*metzarfah*), whereas it should have said "ascribes to him as if he had done it"—see there in *Korban Nesanel*. b) The matter is not that the Name of *Havayah* would be nullified, Heaven forbid, from the two Names of *Havayah*; rather, the discussion concerns the *piseik ta’amei* (the disjunctive cantillation marks) between them, such that in the future, *Havayah* will be one—the two Names in unity. See *Zohar Chadash* 138a, *Likutei Torah* *D’NaT”A*.

(From a letter dated 24 Sivan, 5714)

There is no answer to your letter, in which you write that you are in doubt as to whether my instruction has anything to do with your question.

After asking your forgiveness, I must use the same expression from your letter: it is doubtful whether this has anything to do with your question.

The issue is not whether one can know *Torah Shebichtav* by heart, which comes from studying it multiple times in a book.

Your question was why one should not establish a practice of learning *Torah Shebichtav* by heart (not necessarily from a book). To this, it was pointed out to you that there is a *psak din* (halachic ruling) not to do so. The primary source was also pointed out, but this is also a law in *Shulchan Aruch* (Orach Chaim 49).

All the examples you bring—that *Tanaim* and *Amoraim* knew verses from *Tanach* by heart—is truly a waste of effort, for in every *shul* you will find Jews who know *Ashrei* by heart, and we are not even speaking of *Krias Shema*, even though everyone knows that this is *Torah Shebichtav*. But as I said earlier, knowing by heart is one thing, but studying by heart as a fixed practice is the essence of *Torah Shebaal Peh*, not *Torah Shebichtav*.

It is even more surprising and strange, according to your writing that you go through the *Tanach* every two months, how you can ask for an answer before you have delved into it...

(From a letter dated 19 Elul, 5717)

(From a letter dated 28 Iyar, 5716)


## פרשת פרה — פרשת החדש

## 284

### Parshas Parah — Parshas HaChodesh

...To conclude with a thought that mirrors the opening: It is well known that the Yerushalmi in Megillah (Chapter 3, Halacha 6) states that one should not interrupt between Parshas Parah and Parshas HaChodesh. Based on the mnemonic that this corresponds to the third and fourth cups of the Seder night—the time of our freedom—it is understood that there is a quasi-prohibition involved in doing so. It was said at the farbrengen of this Shabbos that this can be explained as being founded upon the words of our Sages (Sanhedrin 97b): "If Yisrael performs teshuvah, they are redeemed." Further explanation and clarification is added by the Rambam (Hilchos Teshuvah, Chapter 7, Halacha 5): "And immediately they are redeemed." This is cited by Rabbeinu HaZaken, the author of the Tanya (who decides the hidden aspects of Torah) and the Shulchan Aruch (who decides the revealed aspects of Torah), in his Iggeres HaTeshuvah, Chapter 11: "They are redeemed immediately."

(From a letter dated 27 Adar, 5715)

## אלעזר, ר&quot;א הקפר

## Elazar, R’ Elazar HaKappar

 The Gemara relates that R’ Elazar HaKappar taught: “A person should always view himself as if he is standing on the edge of a sword.” 

Seemingly, this instruction is difficult to understand. Why would one be required to view himself in such a state of constant peril? Furthermore, how is it possible to maintain such a state of mind in a practical sense, given that a person must also engage in his daily affairs and live with a sense of relative stability?

However, with the understanding of the *avodah* of a Chassid, we can explain this. 

The *avodah* of a Jew is to constantly strive for *dveikus* with Hashem. This *dveikus* is not merely a static state, but a dynamic movement of *ratzo v’shov*. A person must always be in a state of *bitul*, recognizing that his entire existence is dependent upon the *Ohr Ein Sof*. 

To "view oneself as if standing on the edge of a sword" means that one must realize that the boundary between *yesh* and *ayin*—between the illusion of independent existence and the reality of *Elokus*—is as thin as the edge of a sword. At every moment, a person is suspended between these two realities. If he leans toward the *yesh*, he risks losing his *hiskashrus* to the source of life; if he leans toward *bitul*, he achieves the true purpose of his creation. 

Thus, this is not a state of fear or anxiety, but a state of heightened *kavanah*. It is the recognition that every action, every word, and every thought is a decisive moment in the *avodah* of *is’hapcha*—transforming the darkness of the world into a dwelling place for Hashem. By maintaining this awareness, a person ensures that his *avodah* is not merely habitual, but is characterized by the intensity of *mesiras nefesh*.

## ארגמן

## Argaman

The word *Argaman* (purple) is composed of the letters *Alef, Reish, Gimmel, Mem, Nun*. Our Sages explain that these letters represent the four kingdoms that subjugated the Jewish people: *Alef* for Bavel (Babylon), *Reish* for Madai (Media), *Gimmel* for Yavan (Greece), and *Mem* for Edom (Rome). The final letter, *Nun*, represents the future kingdom—the kingdom of Mashiach—which will rise and endure forever.

Seemingly, this requires clarification: Why is the concept of *Argaman*—which signifies royalty and majesty—associated with the four kingdoms that oppressed the Jewish people? Furthermore, why is the future kingdom represented specifically by the letter *Nun*?

The explanation lies in the fact that the *avodah* of the Jewish people throughout the long *galus* is to extract the "sparks of holiness" (*nitzotzei kedushah*) that fell into the *kelipos* of these four kingdoms. Through our *avodah*—specifically through *tefillah* and the performance of *mitzvos*—we elevate these sparks and transform the darkness of *galus* into light.

This is the deeper meaning of *Argaman*: The *kelipos* of the four kingdoms are not merely obstacles; they contain within them the potential for holiness. When a Chassid engages in *avodah* with *mesiras nefesh*, he reveals that even within the "purple" of worldly royalty and power, there is a hidden spark of *Elokus*. By refining these sparks, we complete the *birur* (refinement) of the world, which leads directly to the revelation of the fifth kingdom—the kingdom of Mashiach, represented by the *Nun*, which denotes the *nefilah* (descent) that is transformed into an eternal *aliyah* (ascent).
